O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have finished this book which is the last of the science of medicine assembled from its precepts and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to my mind that I must finish this treatise which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, surgery
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fraught in our region and is rare throughout, if it is deprived of science and care, and only remains the small descriptions in the books of the ancients that the hands have performed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the emptiness, and are closed the understanding and is alienated the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I can bring it to life together the order of this treatment in accordance with the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and the other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it befits him who enters this to learn in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he has judged the bones, and the forms and the connections and the separations of them, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and limbs and the number of joints, and the movement of the veins and the rest, and of their issue.</start_of_turn>
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates said that the pain without the disease is like the work without the art; and the same in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say at the beginning of this book that he who is ignorant of the things that are before him, if he is rash and does not reflect, will often do more harm than good; as I have seen many times with these matters that are concerned with this science and if he neglects science and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a madman who drank wine mixed with vinegar for scrofula or the swelling of a woman’s uterus, and cut the arteries of the neck; and as much blood flowed out as for a woman to die between her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another time a stone came out of a bladder of a sick man, and the stone was great; it carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and was dead for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I heard it already called for the treatment, and saw the condition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and so I knew that if I cut it out he would die.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another time a maid came to take care of our lord who had a broken limb, and with the splinter caused a wound; and the physician's knowledge was strained by the fracture above the wound as if by strong binding, and did not allow blood to flow from the wound, and left it until the end; and he commanded that it should not be moved again; and it happened that when the limb was finally freed and the splinter was taken out, it was lost.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I beseech you to come here, and I hasten to come and loosen the limb; and when I see it dislocated, it is without pain and without suffering.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way the corruption has already been confirmed or the limb is unsound, and it will not recover; and the corruption will continue to rise in the limb as long as the limb is entirely lost.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another mire which effracts the abscess, encloses it, and then inflames it by the malice of its lordship.</start_of_turn
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the swelling, when it is full of melancholy humor, it does not suffice to touch it with fire except when it is in a part of the body where one can remove everything that is corrupted.</start_of_turn
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, take heed, for the work of hands has become divided into thirteen parts: that is to say, there is danger in many ways; and I shall show in each chapter where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, you must always be wary, lest the fools speak falsely of you.</start_of_turn>
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your arms in custody, and undertake your patients calmly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you may come out whole and sound; and let the dangerous diseases be banished by health; and abstain from your arms from anything that makes you doubt, and hold fast to your life so that you can go from this world to the next in peace.</start_of_turn>
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	Galens speaks in verses of his admonitions: “Do not take my advice carelessly for any disease, for you are called foolish if you do.”
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with the cautery of fire and dry medicine, and this chapter orders from the head downwards; and the forms of instruments, and the materials of cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with the dressing and piercing of wounds, and the treatment of abscesses, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter orders the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and sprains, as well as other things; and it is ordered from the shoulder joint downwards, and from the form of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Neither do we recall from our work what is the quality of the aid and the great discomfort of a complexion like this.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the discomfort, is the longest word and the subtlest science and the most secret response; and about this many have spoken, and they agree on this; and I am stifled by their words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for any complexion or where there is matter, for there are two kinds of complexions: that is to say a complexion that is hot in the sense of matter, and a complexion that is dry in the sense of matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche, assembled matter, some declare that cautery is of great aid; others declare that cautery is of no avail in disease except that which comes from heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be a remedy for hot diseases by heat, nor by drought; and thus those who say the opposite that cautery does great aid in dry and hot diseases that arise from the humors of the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it to be otherwise by experience.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, there is no other way for me to know of this matter except by experience, for I have long observed the chapter of cautery in the books, and the diversity of temperaments of men, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and their issues and remedies; for other temperaments I have no knowledge, even in cold and wet diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agree and are accustomed to the cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, lads, that fire cautery with secret cures is better than burning cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery is simple, and brings no further pain than to the limb that is being treated, and harms no other part besides that.</start_of_turn>
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one limb to another, causing grief and bringing about diseases of the limb; and often cause harm to the patient.</start_of_turn
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire in its height and by the goodness of its substance does not cause this, if there is no excess.</start_of_turn>
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And that which I have said to you I have found through experience and through the length of my service and study in this art, and it is confirmed by truth; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to conceal the secret which is reported or fiery, and the quality of work, as it demonstrates the cure of diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; or you may consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know this, child, that it is in what degree the cauteries must be made that they agree, and when they are pricked.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is useful in all degrees, for the harmful effects that arise from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and even if the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot await the degree that is more harmful to the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, my son, that the foolish people are right; for the disease which is cured by cautery never returns; and he says so. But it is not so that they cure, for cautery is but a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for its promptness of action, and for the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And indeed, there is one thing that is certain: the disease never returns according to the complexion of the patient and the course of the disease and its power; and there are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and other things, except when cautery is administered in place of these or when there is little superfluity and moisture, for indeed, in such cases the pain does not return any more; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And indeed, many people do not understand that cautery is called the last resort of medicine; but they see; but they do not believe that cautery is better than medicine, but their understanding is false, for indeed, cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we have administered other treatments in any disease and they have not been successful, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, though cautery is behind medicine, it does not accord with the intentions of the wise.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients say that gold cautery is more effective than iron, because of the quality of the gold and the excellence of its substance; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not cause harm, but this is not true, for I have proved it, and have found that it is seen in many people; and gold cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is charred by the color of the gold and when it has cooled down; and if you burn it too much, there is enough hindrance.</start_of_turn
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery as we have learned it to be useful in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter from head to toe, because in this way the patient will find it easier to recover.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Olive oil cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and there are many causes of this disease called "soda," and also from many humors that descend from the head as sweat, and from many dreams and pain of the teeth and throat, and even from many diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	If the patient is purged by medicine that softens the head of the bone, two or three times, according to what the physician deems useful, agreeable and customary for the patient, then make him cough up the head of the bone again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make him sit comfortably between your hands, and put his hands over his head; after that place the root of your thumb on the root of his index finger between his two thumbs; and there where your two middle fingers will be, if it bleeds from the root then withdraw the cautery which is called "olive," for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put away the sign of ink; and make an incision and extract the hand a little and a little, and then fix your hand steadily, and repeat the cautery until you see the bone somewhat; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take one mouthful of silk and put on gauze, and take away the wound, and leave it for two days; after that put on a soft dressing.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the old folks, the more time the wound stays open, the more it purges; and for this reason it helps to move.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say, none of these people say that we must leave the cautery on for so long that part of the bone is burned, and then we must close what is burnt of the bone, and be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say others that we must leave the cautery on for so long, and press so hard that it breaks as wide as a woman’s girdle for this reason that the humors issue outwards; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; after that we must cure and bind.</start_of_turn>
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem to me to be very good in all cases, for some men or because of fear; and I believe that I ought to leave it alone; for the head of the shoulder is easily loosened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and even when the head of the shoulder is weak by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more salve and soothing for me, and for this reason I shall do this in this case.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times, pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain in the head that lasts a long time, the physician should use poultices, herbs called "cochie," and purges of head, oil, and plasters; and if we apply the cautery as we have said above, it is of no use.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Be careful if the patient's condition is serious and that it is not too painful; otherwise, cauterize only as much as we have said above.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have cauterized the area around the head bone as we have said, cauterize the vein which is called "vasselz"; and hold your hand over it so that you do not see blood until you reach the bone: the patient experiences more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is better to cauterize the edges than the middle of the wound.</start_of_turn
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the shoulder there comes sudden pain, and the disease extends up to the head, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by medicines that are modified, and other cures have been made as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this has not profited: then one must make cautery according to two methods, that is to say by means of medicine and of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine cautery is like this: if you take an alder root, and rub the skin and cover with it. If there are two heads, do the temple or where the pain stays in its part as much as you can to reattach the alder root under the skin; and when it is reattached, if you bind it and stretch it well and leave it for fifteen hours; then take it out and treat the root with vinegar and leave the wound for one or two days; then put on a bandage that will cover the wound until it is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the wound is cured while it is still sound; and if you see that you do nothing of those medicines which I have written or dose to treat with burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is as follows. Shape it like this:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And is called "clos" because its head is made in the shape of a cauldron or pot with a little lip in the middle; grasp the painful area and hold the iron slightly lower than the thickness of the skin; and when half of the thickness of the hair has been burned, release your hand when the artery is not burnt, and there will be plenty of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After putting on cotton wool, remove the flesh from the wound by two days; then put on moist cotton wool, and then cure the wound until it is healed; and if you are going to cauterize this ulcer with the cautery that is called "cultellare", at the tip, and keep the artery covered in this ulcer that is not ancient.
de emigraine	De Emigraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you have finished treating the emigration, as we have said in the sections on diseases, and you see that the cautery has not helped, and that the patient still suffers, then you must omit the cautery which is called the "cultellare" while it is blunt; and mark the skin with a line half an inch long, and hold your hand once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and that the blood does not flow until the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when you move it, and that the patient does not have regret except for the spasm and the pain that comes from the spasm itself, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or from its cutting, for there is great danger and even for the one who does not know it, and who has not studied and is not experienced; and leave the work in peace; but I will tell you later how to retain the blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it is described.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the area as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see that this is of no use, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has a pair of tweezers; this is a better cautery than the previous one and is more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the cold of winter the ears suffer pain.

de la torture de la bouche	from the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is not other than those which move from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery which has the appearance of those which come from drying and hardening of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture which moves from phlegm of hydras and evacuations of head and vomiting, and this is worth nothing, then you must cauterize the patient with three cautery instruments: one at the root of the ear, and the other a little below the temple, and the third between the two eyebrows; and put the cautery over the part which opens well, and make the cautery in the place where the head of the ear is below a little of the edge of the ear, and another in the temple as long as a bean; and leave the cautery there until half of the hair is burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is like the little cutter which we have put before you, but it is a little more subtle and it is better that the knife be a little thicker; after curing like this as I have said, until it is well healed.

When epilepsy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, and it brings no profit, and the patient has no fever, then make three cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the place which is called "vasselz" as we have said before; and the fourth cauterization on the back of the stomach. And be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	When epilepsy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, and it brings no profit, and the patient has no fever, then make three cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the place which is called "vasselz" as we have said before; and the fourth cauterization on the back of the stomach. de l’epilempsie	De l’epilempsie.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should only use fire cautery when it is suitable for the patient, and before that they must modify the brain by other means when the patient is great and suffering from excessive medical care.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a young child who cannot endure suffering, make them gargle and chew, modifying the brain often with bones of meat; after that, let the patient breathe calmly and then perform the cautery as we have said before, on the veins and arteries; and if the patient is strong and suffering, make cauteries as we have said for those with paralysis and softening of bones, on the spine of the back and neck, or the olive cautery as we have mentioned.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make the cautery subtle as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie. After that, take the patient’s head; then make a circle of lint well made, like a circle, and put it on the head; and keep the patient’s limbs crossed, and hold them firmly from all sides; then show the limb and let some old rue de berbis pour it; and burn it with moderate heat, so that it can endure; then take out the circle from the head and let it cool down; do this to the patient every week once with another good diet, until he is healed.</start_of_turn

de l’awe des eulz	Or if you see the burn cauterized with making several points throughout the burn. This method of cautery soothes the brain instantly; then put on moist cotton wool in the wound and grease with gelline.

When the pain first appears, as signs indicate which I have said in the division, then begin and make the patient drink something that purifies the head, and keep him away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times without food.

dou cors des larmes	And I will teach you how to extend the arteries in the extraction and how to cauterize it; and in no case shall you make the cautery or hatereil of bones behind the joints of the tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere. dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Pain de larmes par dedens les eulz

dou poil qui point l’oil	And if you see that you must perform two cauteries on the two nipples which are as long as the nipples themselves; do not leave your hand until a third part of the areola has burned, as I have said.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never is it that the hairs of the nipples are converted to beards, and prick the oil, and thereby make cauteries in two ways: that is to say by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then command the patient to keep the hair long; after that mark upon the hair a figure that is as much like the fuel of a mouse as possible, or as the beginning of a sign beyond the hair; then put a soaked rag in butter and a little salve on the oil, and cover the cautery like this:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have marked, and doing it several times, so that the burn is neither too deep nor too shallow; and the sign of the work is that the scab retreats, and the hair is raised to the point of the oil; then take your hand away, and leave for two or three days; then put a soaked rag in butter until the scab has hardened; after that treat with oil until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	If thereafter these hairs reappear, and the burn is softened, repeat the cautery on the same limb as before; and if the hairs are scorched, burn until the burn returns to its natural state, and is even, and do not prick the hairs with the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fiery cautery of medicine is that you command to the patient that he let the hairs grow long and even, then make a mark of the shape of a laurel leaf; then take French soap and live chaff, each a third, and grind them together well; and make it hot, if it does not cool, and put it on the mark that you have made like a laurel leaf, and put the burn on the patient’s eyes; and if the disease persists with only oil, if you must open in oil, and if in both; and put cotton wool soaked in egg white on the wound. And the head of the patient must be in its place and put your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once or twice whenever the patient feels a biting sensation of the medicine, for he feels the biting sensation as well as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine has reached your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting has passed, if you lift the limb up, and you see the wound raised as much as if it had been raised by the contraction of the fire or by an incision; and if it is firm, it is well. If not, repeat the remedy above the limb or the remedy has not worked, until your works are equal, and your wounds are well-stitched; then put on a wet bandage over the wound until the swelling has gone down, and then cure the wound which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you have taken great care of your work with great care so that it does not need any medicine at all. And if the wound becomes soft afterwards, and the hair is pricked in the oil, repeat the remedy above that wound which has become soft from the wound itself; then cure until it is healed; and that is the form of the chasteberry fruit.</start_of_turn>
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the souls of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to that be their restrictions; and do not be afraid to take the right way to the one who is the student of this art.</start_of_turn>
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure for fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then you must cauterize according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to hold his limb steady; and hold his limb between your hands in a firm manner so that it does not move, do not let it hang down; then put a moist cloth or paste of persicaria over the oil; then burn the cautery which is part burned: and it is held to the limb as if it were a pine cone, gather up what is split. If you see that any hair is pulled out from one end to the other, or if you see that there is any attempt; but all this is worth more than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula until it is over, and in traction remove the pus, and dry; and if it is closed, if the work is done, and draw out the wound; then put the cautery on the burn and hold your hand to the cautery at the part where there is no nerve exposed only by oil, that your hands do not make a tremor; and put the cautery in the grease of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you approach the fire cautery at the outset until the bone, that would be best. If this does not suffice, repeat the cautery once more; otherwise, if you have labored over it, leave it for two days. Then put on moist cotton wool in the wound and treat with an desiccant until it is healed. If twenty days have passed and it is still not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and then follow what is customary in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a manner of cautery of fistula which none of the ancients have mentioned. Understand fistula, and open the vessel; then put in the slit one spoonful of camphor which is like this in form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and do the quantity of a third of a plum; and hold your hand or palm firmly, and do not move the patient in any way, until the melted wax has run out; and then it is convenient to put on the oil over the patient's cotton wool in abundance, on wax or on earth: the wax will thus adhere to the fistula and the patient will recover with great ease and delight.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, that is good. If not, if it must be administered through the neck, and return the fistula to its original place as it should be in its proper place.

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the armpit.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes to the root of the arm or in the elbow, or in the jaw, or there are roots of teeth, after doing so it becomes putrefied and rotten and is swollen and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in the sections above, and it does not profit: therefore you must have .i. a burn according to the quantity of the fistula; after the breaking or cutting of the fistula, and hold your hand until it is finished from front to back; and do it once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the limb and remove the corrupted bone, as you would do in its chapter.</start_of_turn>
dou movement des dens	Pain de mouvement des dents
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you have treated it with medicine but it is of no avail, then put the patient's hand in your own; afterwards remove the cautery whose form will arise later in this part as if you put a bandage over the tooth; and put the cautery into the tooth cavity thoroughly, and hold your hand as long as the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; then fill the patient's mouth with salt and keep it closed for an hour and a quarter.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this part, if the tooth which was moving is confirmed, and the soft tissue is restrained, and the moisture is corrupted, dry.
de la dolor des dens	Of toothache.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize in two ways: burn cautery and fire cautery.</start_of_turn>
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Burn cautery: if it is like taking burr from a blister, and the end put in a spoon of iron or tin; after take cotton and wrap over the tip of a rag, and the blister boils, and put on the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cold; and do this often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth.  And if you see if there is much pus and cotton in the burr, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the iron again until the fire comes to the cheek of the tooth.</start_of_turn
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Fire cautery: if it is like taking a cane of iron or tin, and either thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heat the cautery, as it will be shaped later, and put on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cold; do this often, for the pain will be the same or more. And it is recommended that the patient fill his mouth with good burr in the haste of this cautery, and then take hold of it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And do the cautery as you wish, and according to what you are able; and this is the form of the pain.
des scrophules	And do the cautery as you wish, and according to what you are able; and this is the form of the pain.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is caused by cold moisture and is not subject to digestion by medicines, then you must cover the burn with a cloth, for otherwise there will be swelling; make an incision on the side away from the burn, and put the burn on the abscess once; if there is mixing, do so until the abscess is almost healed; if the abscess is small, put the burn on as much as the quantity of the abscess allows, and leave it for two days; then cure the wound of boils and stitches when it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores, and even when this comes from a cold complexion, then you must first relieve the patient with solvent medicines; then make the burn at the root of the throat, and keep it from going too low, and do not burn anything except the ulcer; then make another burn at the joint of the collarbone and the base of the spine, which is called the "claw" because of its shape; and cure the wound as described above until it is healed.
de la toust	De la toust.

de ydropisie	De ydropisie

de la menoison	De la menoison.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When cold and moist urine comes from the belly, and the retaining and digestive virtue which is the stomach and intestines is evacuated, and cannot be cured by means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having great appetite, if you do not do.i. great cautery on the stomach as it has been said above or cautery of the stomach, with the circulation of the cautery; and .iiij. cauteries around the spleen all at once.i. cautery of the umbilical cord and .ij. cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, do cautery on the navel and .i. one cautery on each side, and .ij. several small cauteries on the stomach below the great one; for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	De la cure des emorroydes.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are deeply rooted, or several, and are ancient, and are of gross cold and moist humors, which are corrupted; they are cured as we have said in the divisions, and it does no good if you perform cauteries: namely two on the spine of the buttocks, which is all that suffices to expel the feces that obstruct the passage, and to triangulate; and one cautery on the buttock.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. If you think the stomach is becoming cold, and the meat is not cooking, and you see the face swelling up, then on the face you should make one large cautery on the stomach, as we have said before, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen with all the cautery nails; and leave the cautery open for a long time. After curing, keep the body warm until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	From the charnosite which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you touch the "thelul", if you see the burn appears to cut, and then put it all on fire over that "thelul" which is touched; and leave it as long as the burn comes out at the birth of the vein, without cutting; do this once or twice. If there is much "thelul", if you burn each one as we have said; after that treat the wounds that are useful as long as they are healed. And if you burn with a large burn on the fat, there will be more great help.

Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure large sizes or openings, as we have told you, if any disease comes to pass that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When no fistula comes, and it is filled with putrefying and corrupt moisture, if the physician has made every possible attempt, and continues to hold them, remove the cautery that appears to scratch, and insert it into the fistula according to the degree of its tension; and repeat the cautery until the diseased part is stiff and corrupt, once, twice, or thrice, according to the degree of the swelling; and beware of the nerves that are cramped and the large veins. If the fistula is close to the bladder or intestines, be wary of these parts and do not burn them except in charnut form. Think that it is not always necessary; after curing the disease as much as possible, if the parts are relaxed and the matter is hardened throughout, then remove the cautery entirely; but if the matter is not hardened, remove only the diseased part, corrupting the bone at the same time; and do so as one of us has said previously.

de la vessie	When pain of fruit comes with heavy rains and strong wind, and does not yield to a woman's talent, then it is proper to cauterize the fruits on both sides with the needle cautery which we mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be two cauteries in a line, and it will be more effective.

de la marris	De la marris.

de la hainche	De la hainche.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac. Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the joints are affected by moisture that is spread throughout the limb and when the pain comes from inflammation, that is called "podagre." de la routure dou syfac	of the route of the face
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the shoulder joint comes out of its socket, and the ball descends like a coon, this is new; if you see the cure for this, do not trust it; and if it uses things that leave the belly open, so that the worms descend from the belly; after that, make the patient sit on his back between your hands, and command him to keep his arm stretched out as long as the ball is repaired, and hold it at your two sides, and mark the exit of the shoulder joint from the bony prominence, and as soon as there is any sign that it is like half of a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	When it is soft and secret, and he sweats, let go of the ball and keep your hand on it so that it does not go back; and take care of the patient’s wounds well, and put on him some lint and some serjeants on the wounds, and another on his palm; then put the cautery on the sign at your whole hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you have reached the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware prudently that the ball does not slip when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or anything worse.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is for nothing. And it is recommended that the cauteries of the small people be subtle according to their measure, and the great people also great according to their measure; after two days cure the burn of the cautery of butter until the scab is bony; after that cure other wounds until they are healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is recommended that his diet should be scanty, so that the ball does not slip when he moves from his bed to the chamber.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, he will find a well-formed scab, which will last for forty days; and he will have had good rest, so that he will work steadily and take care not to eat too much or drink too much, and not to smoke too much; and when he has followed this teaching, he will be entirely healed. And I will speak of the treatment of boils in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, he will find a well-formed scab, which will last for forty days; and he will have had good rest, so that he will work steadily and take care not to eat too much or drink too much, and not to smoke too much; and when he has followed this teaching, he will be entirely healed. Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When wounds come in other parts and are well-known, and you see that they do not grow further, then you should make a burn with the cautery according to their quantity; and either a third or a fourth of the wound should remain unburned. mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	But first mark the place with a mark and make a line parallel to the breadth of the wound, and another perpendicular, and hold your hand firmly against the cautery clamp. But the first cauteries are lighter and more fluid.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in no limb, whether from swelling or injury, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medicine does not suffice, then it is advisable to cauterize with the cautery known as "points," and to cauterize according to the length of the limb and the smallness and weakness and toughness and twisting of the joint and the degree of pain. If the first cautery is successful, well and good; but if not, repeat the process. Indeed, it is customary to cauterize the part that is nearest to the ailment, for it is believed that this will ensure that the cauteries are effective until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	From meselerie
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	From meselerie. The sickness is never aided by fire cautery. Indeed, the very disease comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take warning if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, do not linger or delay, for you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the whole sickness, whereupon you will make five cauteries upon the head: one at the nape of the neck, the other towards the front at the end of the beard; and two on the two corners, and one behind the ear; and leave your hand there as long as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the pus comes out forcefully so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse as it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered everywhere; and it appears manifestly, if you must cauterize from these cauteries which we have said or from the chief, and one cauterize in the neck, and two on the spine of the collarbone, and three on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and one other in the groin, and two on the shoulders, and two on the tendons of the arms and legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet; and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, that you do not burn them; and never make the cautery on the bone of the heel, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. The hairs that are made long by the fire cautery grow more and more useful; and the patient does not feel pain from the fire cautery as he would from a wound, for the flesh is already corrupted. And it is necessary that the fire cautery be great and small according to the limbs and joints, as you do with herbs. After treating with flour of times with honey and other remedies until it is healed.

When swelling comes to no limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not well, then one must make cauteries on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either the cauteries should be made at a distance from the bone, or at the very least as close to the bone as possible. And one must not make the cauteries on the hand, foot, or back, except in the case where the nerve is cut that makes the limb immobile. And in such a case, all other parts must be known in relation to the limb and the movements of the nerves that move the limb.
de albaras	De albaras.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and the physician's remedies are of no avail, then a cautery is to be performed once with a little burn, according to the quantity of the black bile which has come, until the blenchour is bony and its color is altered; then it is to be treated with flour of times, lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and saffron and alum, one part of each; mix them all together and bandage them with a cloth, and keep them until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for fistula by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre. When a boil starts to come, and you see it stop, if you burn it with a cautery that looks like a circle, all around the boil. li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Another method of disease that is called "corrodens," and is nothing other than a weakening of the limb, for it breaks the limb as fire breaks the dry lines. If you see this disease in the body which can suffer from fire cautery, then immediately burn the cautery small and large, according to what is appropriate to the body or the disease; after the cautery of all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and nothing remains except what is not corrupted. And then leave it for two days, and put on the burnt limbs that it is sore with oil until the fiery boils are ossified, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure of the oily inflammation. And if after two days that the char remains not healed, this is good; and if this is not the case, repeat the cautery on what remains corrupted. And this weakening is never cured by means of medical treatment instead of fire cautery; but every kind of fire cautery is of greater help, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Hair that comes out whole like nails.

li cure dou trembler	The cure for tremors.

Sometimes appear by discharge the body bathes, or pusules full of pus, which come from corrupt matters.
