And in no case should it be begun when they appear, according to this manner, and it does not prevent the discharge of blood, but is broken by the surplus from which it comes, and is cured; but it is necessary that this should be done after the evacuation of blood.

Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag le second livre des cures de taille.

We have already said in the first chapter that in all diseases where it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or to apply warming medicine, and to inquire into the lesions and their causes, and the instruments and forms of cautery; and in this chapter we will speak of the most legitimate way to proceed in this work, since we have found it to be lighter in this way than in any other way.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	Moreover, as I have said at the beginning, it is necessary to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapters of the cautery, and for this reason it is necessary to exercise greater caution.</start_of_turn
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not be reckless. For many people have come to harm through their diseases; some of whom, when they suffer greatly from their ailments, grow reckless and blame their suffering on the severity of their disease. From such people we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these there are some who will tell you: "Wait, I am wise"; and the disease is dreadful. dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have ordered thee this chapter by chapters, according to what is before or after the cautery, that I have ordered thee from the head down to the toes, because thereby thou shalt find it more conveniently than what thou hast to do.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Saiches that this disease comes out many times at childbirth, and when the babe’s bail is strained too strong the head of the babe; and never comes from a known cause except that one does not know it.</start_of_turn>
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease vanish except in the spring, and with all that I have heard, it seems to me that it is worth leaving the work in parts for cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen many times in my childhood when the head of the shoulder was dislocated due to moisture, and the head grew so large that it could not support itself; and I believed so much moisture that it became blood, and this moisture if it is gathered between the bones above the scapula, between the shoulder blade and the arm; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the shoulder blade and the arm, and the incision is small, that you must make a wide incision; and be as long as .ij. we have seen, until the moisture has gone; and when this is done, the shape of the scapula will be like that of a spindle.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture is excessive and swells the bone, and if you see the corners of the bone protrude in the lower part, and if it causes pain that increases when you press your hand inwards, and this does not subside: if you suspect that the bone is fractured, make two incisions as described in this manner.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision, drain out the moisture forcefully. Then bind the incisions with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave for five days. Then remove the dressing, and cure the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the limb elevated, and feed the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed.</start_of_turn>
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another method of incision is to look or open the apex of the abscess, and gather the fluid; for it is never in front; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.</start_of_turn>
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.
de reume	When the shoulder joint is dislocated and the opening is wide, and the injection of liquid, and you do according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known ailment that is called "cataract," and there are pus or white spots, and the disease is ancient, and the medical cure does not help, then the only remaining cure is to cauterize with that which covers the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief. Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood spurts continuously upwards, keep pressure on it without interruption.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open on sensing it, if you think it is two fingerbreadths wide, mark its end and advance until bone is reached; what is to be done with blood that spurts out if it is more than two fingerbreadths, or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the edges of the incisions do not reunite, then strain the wound and ligate it, and cure it with dressing until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on sensing it, if you think it is two fingerbreadths wide, mark its end and advance until bone is reached; what is to be done with blood that spurts out if it is more than two fingerbreadths, or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the edges of the incisions do not reunite, then strain the wound and ligate it, and cure it with dressing until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes, and acute fever, because of tears and the heat in temples and old saliva forsened and similar things, it is treated by means of medical cures and everything that does not help, if we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus the manner of extracting them is that the patient should make the hair of his temples grow long; and he should understand the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating; and is much more easily restored than in some men who are too cold. And if it is restored, he should strain his neck the patient of some cloth, then wipe the area with no rough cloth, and raise the area with warm water until the artery opens openly; then take the sponge which is like this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then he should gently stretch the skin until you see the artery, and then pull it high towards the pincushion, and withdraw it well from the tissues that are under the armpit; and if the artery is tense, if it has a bulge at the tip of the bone, then press that part according to the amount of pain. For if it is not pressed, it will not jump out without pain all at once.</start_of_turn>
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Then he should drain blood from the armpits, up to two inches; and if the artery is large, it is expedient to ligate it with two strong silk threads, so that no blood will be seen in front of the wound, and the blood will drain away; then cauterize the surplus that is between the two ligatures in that place, and then, if you see, burn the hair with a fine cautery until the hair is cut; and this is the best remedy, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.</start_of_turn>
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is helpful to finish off moisture: for this is more helpful with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is useful to extract the arteries that are full of fat and put on well-made stitches; and when you take them out, if you are cured of dry medicines that cause char and stitches, as long as you are sane; and if without support of the artery as you must do if you do this too quickly, or if you touch the vessel with the vitriol, it will stain your hand; and if you do not have this, you must take out the vessel until it is frozen, and rise the cold water until it stops, and strain as much as it is possible; and what is more limp and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery at a distance of .ij. inches, but the incision must be well spaced to prevent lasting too long its heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch; and when you have marked the area with a needle, you must let the fire burn until it reaches the bone, and then close the vein with one inch of leathers; and let the hair be plucked out between the needles, for it is not soldered by this cautery in any way; and this is the form of the fire cautery.
des larmes	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch; and when you have marked the area with a needle, you must let the fire burn until it reaches the bone, and then close the vein with one inch of leather; and let the hair be plucked out between the needles, for it is not soldered by this cautery in any way; and this is the form of the fire cautery.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the test of the chief of force, and it does no good to medicine what is done with it, and you see the face of the patient to be twisted, and feels or front of ambulation as if of a madman; and though they are tense and moist if the hair of paper is held close, and are scattered the papers, and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is any hope of this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it the ancient "cure contuse," and you must make at the patient who has this ailment the hairs that he has over the front, then make two incisions or an even front according to the length of the front; and let one incision be as much as one-third of the front, swallowing down juice until it is level, and the other one-third has one-third of the ribs below the papers, and keep the incision of the arteries that are one-third below the papers; and align your hand from the continuation of the mandible, and let there be some wound according to the quantity of two-thirds that must go through the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have shown a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe the blood, then tighten the clot firmly from one-third of the way so that this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the marrow that is between the two incisions to the outer surface of the bone, then make the other half of the wound until the other second, and then pull out this clot.</start_of_turn>
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the "cultellaire," and is very well grooved on one side, and on the other side is smooth, is not deeply grooved, and that is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If in the first incision the instrument which is called the "cultellaire," and is very well grooved on one side, and on the other side is smooth, is not deeply grooved, and that is its form.
dou reume des eulz	because of the return of the blood
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no acute cautery is used, and you see the eyes tense and small, and the pupil dilate, and the papers burn; and the hair cries out, and where the chief has been pricked, there is great pain, and the patient coughs; then from these accidents arise matters and catarrh which do not come from many veins, but from many blood vessels.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Command the patient to wipe his brow, then make a large wound from the left temple to the right temple, and from there to the bone. That is to say. From the incision of the left temple to the right, go down to the bone; and grasp the nerves of the temples that move with swallowing. When the bone is exposed, drain all the blood from the wound with a sponge, then remove the clot between the two layers of the wound and put in cotton wool. Then cover with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and keep it dry. When it has healed, it is necessary to rub the bone until it begins to grow, and then cure it with drying things that cause the hair to fall out.</start_of_turn>
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In part: take .ij. parts of wheat flower and .iiij. parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to cause the hair to grow throughout.</start_of_turn>
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes pain in the ears is one of three things: grains, or boils, or stone or similar objects like iron; or seeds, like lice, beans, peas; or fluid things like vinegar and urine and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to a stone or other object that does not fit into the ear, do not put your finger in the ear. If you see a stone, if there is no discharge of violet oil or lavender oil, then seek extraction; and let him vomit of concoction, and plug the nose when he vomits, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear still. Many times this cure will come out; and if it does not come out, seek extraction with fine needles, as this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by these needles, it is well done; if not, seek extraction with fine needles of double curvature; and if it does not come out by this, make an incision of an inch and a half and cut off the chief of the incision or pierce the ear very deeply, and squeeze out what is around the incision mole if it comes out with the incision; then the pain will disappear, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out partly, take hold of the bone with your thumb and index finger and put under no instrument that has a point for this purpose, and put a patch of cotton around; then press the thumb on the bone or whatever it is, and the pain will go away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in a hurry to make an incision at the ear-lobe along with the abscess chalaz, and spasm, do this: first make the patient comfortable and loosen the hair of the head; then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty or glandular tissue; and let the incision be as wide as a crescent, as long as you live to the bone, and the bone according to your will; and evacuate the pus immediately from your mouth.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If grains are seen which are swollen and inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, administer sponge-rubber tightly according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this incision if you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract the grains with tweezers and suck out the pus, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When the ear is acute, then the patient must immediately apply a compress to the ear and fill it with cotton wool. And whether the pain is on the same side or the other, if the ear jumps for this, that is good. If not, if many stones are taken out according to the length of the ear, then keep them tense and limp, and dig one into the fire; and put the patient one or two of his ears into the fire, and take out the rest from the other side, and fix one on the side which is in the ear; and do this until the pain is all gone. And if you see that the pain is not going away, take hold of one of the ears and burn the other until the pain is gone; then do the same with the other ear until the pain is gone, as we have said regarding the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the ear, if it is of small size, like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, we must feel it, if we must extract teeth; and this is the easiest thing to do in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ear, when you have cured as we have said in the division and or performed distillations, and the cure does not help, if you must know if there are worms, look at the ear in the sun: if there are no worms visible, if the treatment has produced subtle toothaches, and if there are none visible, take the tweezers which are like this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let the dressing be broad and soft. And keep the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then proceed with all the skill; do this often until you see them come out. And if they do not obey to issue, if I am pressed in the cotton as I have said concerning the stone; and if they do not go out forcibly as we have said, if you administer distillations which the ancients have proved useful in the cutting of worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, thus is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let silver or gold be stripped out of eight petty losses, and over this let the distiller be put; and press down with this instrument of lead well made for this purpose. If you see a scraper and wrap around it with cotton from the point forward; then pour out your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the cotton, and put the cotton in the ear; then press down the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand steadily until the oil is distilled or the ear is almost empty. And let the patient feel in the ear, and let the distillation be neither too hot nor too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same thing happens as adults with wounds or tumors that protrude into the ear, for these protrusions never come out of the ear unless they are seen; and never is there such a thing as perfectly formed ears.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Whenever they protrude into the ear without being seen, it is a sign of serious illness in many cases; and in this case it is clear that you put the diseased ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the swelling, if the swelling has filled the whole cavity as far as it can, then it is formed like this:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it greasy or rough before and behind all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the swelling is of a tumor or cartilage of the ear, if you find subtle fractures, and the swelling is slight, as long as the tumor is completely bony
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if swelling arises in the ear, take one small burnisher and heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the ear. If you feel the swelling which the patient feels in the ear, pierce slightly, and keep only the outer part of the ear; then put in the ear a sponge according to the size of the hole, and pour in a little unguent Egyptian.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything until the wound is healed, or take a sponge and soak it in rose-water, and sprinkle vitriol powder on it; and if you see the ear flee, you must remove the sponge and insert another sponge made of rue oil and wax, until the swelling is ossified; then treat it until it is healed
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If discharge of blood comes, immerse a sponge and cover it with cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments which will solidify the discharge of blood which are to administer distillations.
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	From the heap of papers
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without any decor, if the cautery of the lenticular lentil and the cautery after the incision is worth moving; and many times repair, can no longer remain from their root; and when they are cauterized by fire, if they are burned those roots and do not return anymore.
de la gresle	From the bark of the tree.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come papers of blood from eyes that seem to swell in their form and duration; for this is the disease called "granulinea," and is an assembly of great moisture in the marrow below and above; the work is like this: take guard if the granulinea moves from one side to the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make a generous incision, then gently strip off the outer layer, then take hold of the tweezers and grasp. If you do not grasp it in the right direction, you will not perceive the marrow; and if the fracture is great, if the assembly has a structure, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for the marrow will restore itself quickly and cause harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulinea descends downwards from the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the marrow, extend the granulinea with tweezers, grasp and press from one side and the other; and if the marrow is loosened by the incision, this will cause no harm; and when the granulinea is grasped, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the limb of that which causes harm until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	The wax is thick and adheres to the tissues of paper, which is more noticeable in the morning; for in the morning there is abundant mucus in the eyes, and the tears run down the face so quickly that they cannot be seen in the sunlight. Because of this, the eyelids are often closed and the paper dries on the eyelashes, becoming moist with wax that covers the surface. And when you press the hand to the chest and feel the wax between the fingers.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	When the patient puts his hand in his bosom; then take one cloth of linen, and make a circle with your thumb according to the quantity of wax in the chest; then put it on; then press with your thumbs from one side and the other, so that the wax is gathered into a circle; then make an incision about the width of a vein, without making it any larger than the wound made in the vein; and when you have finished, the wax comes out of the incision, according to the form of a white lump of fat.</start_of_turn>
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the lump entirely with a sharp knife between your thumbs, and turn your hand to the right and left as much as possible; and keep that you do not touch the edges, until you have reached the bottom; that you do not stain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the dislocation does not reappear at the start of the wound, if you expand the wound slightly until it opens; then draw out the foreign body as we have said, and moisten with wool and water, and place back in the limb, and strain the bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there are such fools who break their bones and place on it to corrupt the moisture that has gone dry. Then cure it until it is healed. And if it comes to the limb being cut through again, if you cure abscesses that are bursting as much as they are healed.</start_of_turn>
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers</start_of_turn>
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like substances grow hair-like, adjust them from their natural state and they are enveloped; if they prick the eyes, they cause tears and produce various diseases like common weeping and softening of paper and mucus, up to the point of destroying the eyes; and the cure for this is in three ways: either by entire fire cautery, or by water-based medicine as it is before or alongside fire cautery, or by incision and stitching or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s chief in your left hand, then draw out the paper from your right hand; if it is softened, it is well done; if not, if there is an awl with every thread of hair below; either cut the margin of the paper or the hair grows out below those hairs, and draw out one thread at the root of every hair; then press on the lower part of the paper, pressing out the hairs that have been adjusted, over the entire area up to the great tear until the small one; then draw out one thread and put a small patch of cotton and bandage on the paper, then mark on the paper a figure like a spurge, like the spurge of myrtle, and it is enough that the figure be according to the quantity you see raising the paper that is designed for you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a part that has met with great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened; then do over the whole area up to the twenty-fifth lines that you have marked, and from the great tear until the small one; and if there is one of the incisions close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then stretch out the ointment in one of the two angles of the wound, then tighten; then join the two lips with a suture of a needle with every thread of fine silk, and wipe away the blood, and make the excess threads on the two edges of all things sticky, as you see me do; and if you do not see this, if there is no remedy, then leave the suture and the threads for two or three days; then cure the wound with stitches of dry and constricting things, because the paper is renewed at the bottom of the wound and the joining of the two lips, but the suture is useless (as they say the old ones), and this is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: if you mark the mark with a figure that is just like the head of a myrtle berry, as we have said, then you must take two needles and evacuate them according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then close what is above with small forces evenly according to the form that is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, if you take a needle or there is some thread, and you sew it through the mark; and you take another thread of greater length, and the second thread of lesser length, and you assemble between these two the threads equally; then hold your hand equally, and hold all the skin above where you have marked, as we have said, then assemble the two layers of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if there is an abscess at your incision, if you apply grease and other soothing poultices.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hair of the armpit is converted: if you use what we have said of incision; but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for varicose veins is as follows: convert the armpit hair and fat according to what has been said, then make three veins by art, and two fine threads as long as the hair and as wide as a sparrow's foot; and take three hairs from three parts or hold the threads. Then assemble the one and the other securely above what rests on the oil of the hair, and strain the two veins from the two parts forward; and leave it like that for a few days. The leather which has been strained will rot and decay and will become loose, until it disappears by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the swelling has increased, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has healed and the hair has fallen out, they will no longer prick. This is the form of the three veins that you will make according to this figure and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is thus: take a subtle hook, and there is in it a thread of silken thread. Then join the hooks together and do not twist one with the other; and let the length of the threads be equal. Then order in the chase another thread of silken thread briefly, and do not twist them together. Then put the patient's thumb in its place. And let there be no shadow if the work is completed, for it is a subtle and small work. Then draw out the hook at the whole chase until it pierces in the root of the hairs with the natural position. Then withdraw the hair until there remain one or two or three or more. Then withdraw your hand until the vein is fully exposed at the whole chase with the natural position.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from its pierce and you see it by the light of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has healed in its place and the wound has closed.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the coming forth of an ulcer appears in oil, if there are two possible means: one natural, and the other unnatural.  And it arises from a wound, or from a bite or from cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to perform this work is that you make that suture, and dry the flesh of the wound, and put in between layers of linen, and leave it until it is healed; and do not use anything but dry and astringent things in the treatment of it. For if you do this, if the ailment returns worse than before; but there are things that are softening, such as fennel; and vinegar or salt and linseed seed boiled together, and fat dissolved in any oil, and it covers a layer, and treats this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except in addressing this ailment, that it does not return differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	De la char qui vient en l’oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	From the burn which comes from the oil.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn figure in the wound as it should, that is good; if not, take a needle and put it in the wound, and draw out the burn, make two incisions or break off the edges of the burn; and if there are two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make an angle so that when they are joined together, the figure is as that of a letter which does not have a “j” in it; then break that bone according to the quantity of its cost and burn, of that which teaches the burn, then join the two broken parts, and bind them with a thread of linen; then treat this with the medicines that we have said, and of bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a complete incision over the hair and cover with paper; then withdraw between the two books of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know well everything that pertains to making the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is proper in more diverse situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a complete incision over the hair and cover with paper; then withdraw between the two books of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know well everything that pertains to making the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is proper in more diverse situations.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this fracture has happened in the hand, at home in a partial manner that the limb of the patient is solidified with oil, and cannot move or do his natural works, if you must do so, then you must bite the edge of a scraper from the underside of the limb and leave it high up; and extend as tightly as necessary, until you have reached the point where you see the sprain, so that neither the patient can suffer too much pain nor too little, for the patient will not tolerate too little or too much; and your incision, which you should make carefully, must be just wide enough to reunite that which is broken, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and when that is done, reunite all that is broken, and do not wash in salt water, and lift out cold water, and vinegar; then put between the limb and the oil a bandage of linen, and put on top of the oil wool loosely bound in abundance; and after that put on a layer of vinegar and other things that are soothing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Of the oil of the unguel
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that if the patient puts his head in his right hand, then he will hold the eyes; and hold the instrument in your hand, then coil the unguel has small double curvature, and stretch it out; then take a needle, and put in it one hair of horse, or of ox, or of beef, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle once and fix it firmly with the unguel, and pierce it through all the needle, and tie the unguel with a thread and stretch it out, and protect at all low the cost of the unguel which teaches the prunele and the hair to the oil, and leave the nature itself or the mucus, if in the incision there is not the crust of tears usually; and never stretch the unguel only by the incision and the thread, as we have said; then protect all the surrounding area with wool, and this is the form:

And remove the nail slowly, and if you see that it has diminished a little and the edge is pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil bandage made of alum, and red alum and solder, and stamp the oil until the other side is reached; then repeat the other work in the same way until it is entirely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders thee in oil, as with a postulation, then milk, and first cure the postulation by burning it while it is sound, then resume the work as before until it is sound.

de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes from the navel.

de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the bowl of oil is applied. This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not fierce except when the bowl is assembled in oil, resembling descending water, which is not blood; and the manner in which this appearance comes about is that if you make the patient sit down on the seat which appears and is straight, then take hold of his head with your two hands from either side, and move him until you see the bowl coming down towards his eyes; then either bind him, and do not let him descend and remove the light, and see the patient do the same things as before; and if it does not descend by itself, salt which is like water, and when it descends from the bowl is not apparent as we have said. If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the cloth. That is to say, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cloth and the crown, as long as the bowl is there; and when it comes out, distill in the warm oil mixed with honey, or vinegar or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then be cured of another remedy until it is healed.
