Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, if the water returns for a second time, put the force with the instrument. And when it is firmly secured and will not rise, gently remove the instrument slightly by circling your hand back and forth; then pour a little water on it again, and leave the oil out. Then put on clean oil-soaked bandages or lint and tie with the healthy oil. We and those who are with us put on broiled broth with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda will not enter the oil because there are parts of flesh that have too thick hair, it is expedient that you take the instrument which is called the «alberit», which is like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctive solely, and do not linger too long, but make a subtle incision, then insert the almagda as we have said; and when the work is finished, the patient awakens, in whom he sleeps on his back in a gloomy night; and let there be no movement of any kind, and take nourishment easily, and do not move the head to the right or left, and bind according to his disposition until three days; then take it out of the house in the same gloom, and express its gaze, and let him see nothing, and then put it back in place until the seventh day; and do not let me that you do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but it must be that you nourish this, for in this way the pain will subside rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And so, after the incision, blood comes out; therefore take out the oil before the seventh day, and replace it with that which soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, take out the gaze and put on a bandage, so as to cover nothing more; and keep it in this house until it is healed. And then go out of the house and come in, and it will change in this way; and do not let anyone interfere with it in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iraq who said that in his land they used to make an almagda of oil every day, when the pain occurred, but we have never seen or read of it in our land or in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing for us
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of an almond, for he who does not know them will not recognize them; and they are like spiders properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a goosefoot.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	or like the spur of a rooster from the breast.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Or sometimes newly-born or old hairs appear various, as if there were scorpions with mouths like spiders; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with foul matter of a dark color, or if there is hair of a tawny color like sulfur. In those in which there is sulfurous hair and is not entangled, it is to be understood that you must make the patient sit between your hands and expose his nose to the sun; and cover his nose, and spit onto those hairs, and drive them away; then grasp what you have put under the thumb of the subtle gut and hold it until you are certain that that hair is completely broken.</start_of_turn
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the opening has reached its utmost extent, if nothing is left to hold; and if without being warned, or by incision, if any support fails, if it is a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize as much as possible until the surrounding tissue is unstained and all the vessels are closed. Then withdraw or do not withdraw easily or with pain or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If he does not vomit and moisture comes up to the throat, the vomit that is left is sane; if moisture does not come out as it should, there is pus in the bones beneath the skin; therefore, do not put anything into the throat: it is better to give him a mouthful of coarse thread and keep the hands busy, and put between each knot no more space than a thumb and a finger; and put the patient’s hand over the thread at the front and his hand over the mouth at the back, and clamp one after the other as we hold with our thumbs and index fingers; do this until you have clamped that vessel, then pull out the thread, wipe the vomit, moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam and put it back in its place as before; do this for two days or more, until the moisture has eaten away everything that is left of the vessel; and then put in or remove a cautery for several days until it is healed, and if there is any need for calming medicines, use them also. This is the form of the instrument for extracting the head, from which we distill oils and medicines or not.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it may be of silver or of brass, resembling a broad lamp, like a cauldron; and you shall carry it thus; and if you see, make a closed loop, and the instrument will be flat for purging the head; and hold one hand at the head and the other at the mouth to hold when we burn the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the head of the neck a disease which is called "telul," and it grows and becomes great at once, so that it is visible; and for this reason it is necessary that you should begin to seize it at the outset, and break the bone thoroughly, then remove the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in seizing it when it is great, if you take hold of it with force, of foul colour, of bad omen: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a fleshy swelling, for when you seize it once, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the swelling is of soft touch, not of foul colour, you can see that you can seize it all, if you evacuate the patient and seize it without fear, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When solutions of continuance come in one of these wounds, it is of advantage because in certain homes. It is therefore recommended that this not happen to anyone, if you observe that the wound is fresh throughout its extent; and then join the two edges of the wound to a staple, and cure until it is healed. If the edges are already split from one side to the other, if you must escort all the parts of its circumference until they bleed, then reassemble the two edges to a staple, and strain, and sprinkle upon it some dragon’s blood powder and incense; and put upon the powders a piece of absorbent material of great or other kind, and leave it until it discharges by itself, then cure it until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the staple is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we said in the costure of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the edges of the wound.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home in the hands, there are from the thumbs to the little finger nails of varying sizes, some like grains of wheat, minor and greater; therefore when you turn the fingers, make incisions on each nail, and grasp with tweezers and hold in the palm of the hand; then employ the blood from the incision of a broken vein, until it is no longer bleeding; and then withdraw the tweezers easily, and cure the hand of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the ridge of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times appears on the gums a fleshy bulge which the ancients called "albulus"; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the swelling or bleeding to subside; then remove the broken vein or other powdery astringents and drying agents; and if that fleshy bulge recurs after the incision, and happens many times, if you grasp it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Once are gathered at the head of the teeth, between the gums, escorces which are soft and rough; and never are the teeth black and yellow and gray, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are biting; if it is that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulder bones be in their place, and open the gums or the escorces open, until there is nothing left; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other spots, until they are whole; and if one has what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, if it begins again to rise the second and third time, until you have done everything; and teeth that have met with various forms of instruments to redden, as it is shown by the work, for those who have scraped whose teeth have other forms than those which are between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you apparent.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you stay quiet for a long time, because it must not make me do it; for it is a high-quality substance so we have no excuse for making excuses
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that he will endure, then many times the pain will depart from the patient; and care that it be neither too great nor too small, and make the patient groan out; and whatever does not depart with this groan, as long as the malady persists, for we have already done this for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that he will endure, then you must order that the limb be bound firmly around the joint with a strong strap; then place the thumb and little finger at the first and last joints, so that they are well supported; and then firmly bind the thumb and little finger to the limb.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, if the limb is straightened in the direction of the fracture, and if it does not move, take no other instrument and hold the limb loosely with one hand, and move it as you did before. And if the fracture is perceived and broken, if you must cover it, lay cloth or lint over the wound; and if the bandage is applied too tightly, that it does not break the skin; and you must speak softly over the joint to quiet the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with the greatest part of the pain of the first. And take care that you do not do anything like the ignorant layman, who break the limb many times without cause, and do not bring anything but this that we have told you; but they bring about many times by the origin of this great disease from the roots that remain, or from the limb that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the fracture is treated, wash the limb with wine or oil and vinegar and apply plaster of Paris; and if this does not suffice, burn it.</start_of_turn>
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, indeed mute the hands at first, whether with long points and thick sleeves, that they do not double when you draw the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend when drawing, and be of iron well made, and be toothy so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root comes loose when drawing, if you must put out the moist cotton ball from the wound.i.e. as soon as. Then hold the teeth which are left apart like a beak of a thrush; and be made dense like a lime and that is the shape:</start_of_turn
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to endure these tensions, if you must uncover the bark throughout the root, and put the instrument which is called «althali», which is to say a palatine, since this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and bulky if it does not break me, and if the root leaps by this, it is good; if not, if you help with all the instruments, since these shapes will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has .ij. rings, since this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the rank of teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Or other instruments which are before in the rank of teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Or be great and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, if it is small, if the wound has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not follow the natural curve, and its shape is deformed, even in women of childbearing age, if it is dense enough to impede its eruption, it will not rise properly, and it cannot be remedied: therefore it must be extracted. And if it is associated with the tooth, if you take hold of this instrument which has the shape of a small beak, resembling a file, and grasp it with iron tongs, so be it.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the pain persists in the jaws and the hands for as long as the tooth lasts, and because of that you must not move the others, and if it appears, it can be limed, if you file a part of the lime like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is just like filing nails; and while you are filing the tooth slightly in the jaws and hands, if it does not move at all, when you finish the piece at the end there is no raiser, and if the cavity is too deep and it blisters the tongue, if you must file the rough spot so that it is even, so that it does not blister the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth comes loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth comes loose, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient is unable to press upon it without causing pain, you must treat it with restrictive medicines. This is of no avail; if you must restrain it with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and decays, but the gum does not move. Let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth are aligned, take hold of the wire and double it between the two front teeth, then place the teeth between the other teeth, if there is one or more of them, until you see them clearly almost up to the neighboring tooth; then resume the covering until you reach the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and cautiously, so that it does not move; or if you must bind the root of the tooth if it cannot escape. Then close the teeth with the wire and assemble them, and put them back between the neighboring teeth, and keep them in place so that they do not bleed the tongue. Then leave them in place as tightly as possible, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, do it with another wire; if you linger and delay, it will only cause further pain and will damage the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the front teeth, just as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you reset it anew, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and do not let anything interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of a whale bone; put it back in its place or where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and keep it in place for a long time with firm pressure.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Whenever the tongue or the natural cause comes to the loosening of the tongue, that is not born; or by an accident of a deep wound; the work is such that you must cover the mouth of the patient, and put your hand on his tongue, and hold the tongue; then cover the large nerve of the tongue, as long as the tongue is loosened from its dwelling, and if there is any delay or not, and it is from the soiling of the wound, if you touch the wound and cover the nerve; and keep that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which comes from the loosening; and when you have done this, if you lift the rose-colored blood and easily, or cold blood, then put the tongue back in position with a little attempt; and keep the patient still, that the tongue does not move. And if blood comes from the wound, if you take out the glass splinter; and if it does not go away, if you cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; and then cure with other cures until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see red or black or hard pus coming from it, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a fistula; and if it is declining with moisture, if it is spitting blood, if you touch the wound, and deliver from a part and from the other; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a glass splinter until it is clean, and then come back to your work until you have finished everything; then lift the limb easily and gently, and cure with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are often blood clots in the throat which are called "godath", and which are like almonds in size. When you treat them, as we have said in the previous chapter, and they are not healed, take care: if they are small and pale, do not touch them with metal. But if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with metal, even though it may cause the loss of blood; but leave them alone until they are dead, and then you can remove them, or they will break on their own. And if they are white in colour, and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover them, but first make sure that the clot rests and is quiet. Then make the patient sit in the sunlight, and hold his arms by his sides, and cover his mouth with his hands, and press his tongue down with all your might: this is the way. And let it be of silver or of gold like a needle:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... press his tongue down with all your might: this is the way. And let it be of silver or of gold like a needle. Can you press the tongue down with all of this instrument? And you see the clot: take the sponge and press it into the almond, and pull it out more forcefully than you can. And do not put anything on the cloth with it. Then remove the instrument from the clot, as this is the way it is done. The chief is bent in many places, and one part is over the other, and they are very acute, and is made of iron or gold.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with your thumbs, know that this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with your thumbs, know that this is its form: grasp the thumb and index finger together, and when you have grasped one of the thumbs, grasp the other in the same way, and then make an incision and gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when the blood has drained out, if there are still blood clots, either break them up with nutmeg seeds or burn them with cloves of garlic, or fumigate with marjoram, and the like; until the wound is healed; and never again shall there be any further bleeding from the incision except for the two thumbs, if you grasp them just as before.</start_of_turn>
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with a small abscess in her throat; that is to say, an abscess of little consequence; and she could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and died as a result. And the abscess was so high that it had forced down two teeth from their sockets. I therefore took hold of her hand, and put one finger on the abscess and the other on the gums, and then made an incision and garbled the patient with hot water, hot and easy; and when the blood had drained out, if there were still blood clots, either break them up with nutmeg seeds or burn them with cloves of garlic, or fumigate with marjoram, and the like; until the wound was healed; and never again shall there be any further bleeding from the incision except for the two thumbs, if you grasp them just as before.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	From the navel.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And sometimes there is hair or something put on the medicine, as for the hairs of a barleycorn, and put the instrument on all the medicine over the navel; and the patient should be kept still on his side, so that he salivates and mucus comes from his mouth onto the medicine within, if it does not reach the throat, and the barking; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the navel, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it is limp and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see it, take hold and cover it with any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and withdraw the instrument with all its thread from under the cotton, until the cotton is covered over the navel; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry and wipe it away after three or five days. And if you have to repeat the cautery of the medicine, when you repeat it, and after the cautery wipe the medicine inside the navel with cotton wool, and cover what is around the medicine; and rise up from cold water, and be cured of hiccups as long as you are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this method. Take calamine and isope and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs. Assemble all of these together in one pot and put in oil, and boil. And let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot put one instrument that is pointed according to this method.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And be it of silver or of gold, or be one of the nails pressing in the patient’s mouth until the vapor ascends to the eye by the smell, until the eye is mortified; after that it must be repeated often, until the eye is dry, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the outbreak of the hot swelling, for many things happen; and do not do this except at the subsidence of the hot swelling. And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and put in its head a bit of egg-shell, so that the patient’s mouth does not become too hot; for the bit of egg-shell does not make the vapor irritate the mouth, and that is a good cure along with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened to the throat bone or a fish spine, or nothing; so it must be thought that you must do what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, you must make the patient vomit the patient immediately as the meat is cooked in the stomach; for by chance if it is expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to one thread, and then transfix it. And when it comes back, if it is expelled, and then draw it out; and if it does not come out of this, take one instrument of sponge according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for all must live, neither push the bone inwards; and move quickly that the patient may hold the instrument, for it is either loose or the thing is turned upside down; if the patient swallows, or he forces it with all the instrument equally, as much as he can.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for all must live, neither push the bone inwards; and move quickly that the patient may hold the instrument, for it is either loose or the thing is turned upside down; if the patient swallows, or he forces it with all the instrument equally, as much as he can.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And sometimes medicine is useless, as I have said in the previous division, by the treatment of medicines; and when that does not help, then look in the throat of the patient towards the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that I have mentioned. And if you see the bleeding, if it is only a small speck, or if there are faint pulsations that are worth as much. And if that is not the case, if you take a barley chaff and put it in the throat of the patient, then press or bite down on the barley chaff until it is charred; and do this often. And if the patient feels pain all over, then take a full dose of cold water, and cover the mouth and throat, and swallow continuously; and if the bleeding stops when the patient feels the pain, then stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not yield as we have said, if you fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument which I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will soon bear fruit. And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces visible, and let the pot cover be covered with a gauze perceived in the middle, and in that hole let the head of the instrument be; then pour the fumigation, and the patient puts the chief of the cane in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes out until the nausea; and the nausea will now cease, and if it does not yield, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, and eat dirty and foul things, and drink no water; and then it will surely be driven out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument, as we have mentioned, is like tenailles corbes that are put into the throat; and it has the shape of a beak of a thrush, and there is a roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and when this is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	it is the chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Mouth of similar abscesses is, according to what is remembered from one book to another in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways that these are done. One way is like itself, and the other when there is moisture. And the second way is when they are on bones or in the flesh. For the abscesses of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the bones are other than those that come in joints, and the judges make their judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses are not to be pierced, as long as the bone is alive according to its completeness; and if there are some that must be pierced when they are solid, and do not die according to their completeness, like abscesses that are between joints. For when abscesses are between joints, and it is left as long as it is solid, by chance if it corrupts the tendon and nerve of the joint, because of this contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is between the principal member, and if you wait to pierce it until it is measured, if it has gone to the principal member; or it is between the foundation, and if the perforation is not made that it is dead; and it must only be pierced with solid food that comes with digestion, except for that which is between the foundation, that it does not burst, and be prolonged, and form a fistula; and it can never heal in a great end
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It must be known that you should wash the wound of the abscess that has died according to its completeness, when the pain has subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the fading of the pain and redness, and the faintness and tingling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it must be known that you should make the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and the place where it appeared. And let the perforation be of moderate length, and if the abscess is with hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and all bones that are equal or there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure. Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Those who have no head, if there is a superficial abscess, it is proper that you perforate it completely; and it is proper when the abscess is large, and it has coaled great swelling, and you perforate it, if you do not drain all the swelling in that hour, but drain a part; then stamp the abscess until the swelling is gone; do this many times with great care, until the swelling is gone; even if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman in childbirth, or a small child, or an old man decrepit. des scrophules	And the size on the perforated abscess and the moisture, if it is lighter, because they are little of blood. de squinance	And if thou dost cope the swelling, if thou canst gather together the three parts of the wound and bind them now, then there remaineth no surplus because of the greatness of the swelling. Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient men spoke of the size of the gorge; but I have never seen it done in our land, and that is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	Those who are squinting must understand that the epiglottis, which is the slit in the throat, must be freed; and this will not help, for all the veins and arteries in the body are filled with evil at these points which are above the teeth in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.</start_of_turn>
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss which comes from strangulation.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is obvious. When our tongues split the epiglottis, we split them from two circles or three at most, with a slight cut through, between two circles or according to the quantity of the cut on the surface, do not enter the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And thus, if it is convenient with the section of the epiglottis, there is no scar, and the blood vessels are long enough.</start_of_turn>
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is expedient that he extend the skin of the throat to its utmost extent, then cut the vein as far as it goes until it reaches the cartilage; and avoid the blood vessels of the blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the vein itself as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is proved by the section of smoke of the spindle which leaps up from the broken bone, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And it leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound has passed when we doubt strangulation, gather the four limbs of the wound from the shoulder to the heel, and bind them all around with the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause new flesh to grow, as long as it is safe to do so.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The wound should not be opened until the swelling has subsided and the patient is no longer in pain; and if the patient dies or has become paralyzed, the default should be abandoned.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, hold the epiglottis for this reason that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound; and thus death is prevented.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	Therefore, command the old man to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in two or three days.

Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of questioning the abscesses of the knee is that you take more moisture than you find in the abscess, and turn your thumb and index finger, until you know that the instruments have perceived the hair, then that it be in proportion to the greatness of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then draw out the entrails, and be careful that the spur does not burst.</start_of_turn>

et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if afterwards the shoulder does not bring moisture, if the skin is oily, if the latter is done in a cross, and you take hold as hooks, and lightly scorch from a shoulder part and hold the sleeve or where you have grasped it with the thumb;
