et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it lingers a little while, and if you grieve not, employ the wound of some corrosive powders which bite, restrain the wound and apply soothing things around it; and cure it of other cures as long as it is well.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it is great, if cut the three pounds of the wound, and cure it of that which engulfs flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If the vein beats contrary to you or another if you hurry and employ the broth of vitriol broken, and leave it lying for three days or two, as long as the wound bursts, and rest the inflammation of blood; then return to the covering that has departed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of the entromittent instruments, and they are of three kinds: great, middle, and small; and there are four squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, for enclosing the fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are also like needles with which the sorceries are sewn, and are of citrine, or iron, or silver, and must be of a color that is yellow, and are more experienced with black pitch for enclosing the corbes of the fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of boils are like masses of various appearances, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and if boils have two cortices of two manners each,
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of boils are like masses of various appearances, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and if boils have two cortices of two manners each, and are of two manners; or if boils have one cortex and are of two manners, or if boils have only one cortex and are of one manner; all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these boils are trenchant, and there are some that cut only one side, from which we support the flesh, because of this we do not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And among these introspective methods are the elements that are returned to the hands, so that the patient does not lose them through the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three methods: great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	One should use these only in the case of fractures, such as limbs, arms, ribs, abscesses, and similar things;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And never make use of any other small instrument, like the fists, as in this form, because it can cause bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And he must never be placed in the same place where he has previously grasped veins, arteries, and never again in the same way: for in this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never again swell the limbs of anyone as soon as they begin to corrupt, as though they were limbs of women;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	remain steadfast and flee, and those who see them cured, if they are commanded to cease following this fashion from line b to line g inclusive
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and use the medical salve poulating char, then join the two edges of the wound together with suture, and cure until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the breast leans forward and is eased by its greatness, as with women, if the pain is in the.ij. ribs below, by.ij. similar rents.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	And if one holds the other at the end of both, so that the greater line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then stretch the skin between the.ij. arms, and oil the fat, and mix in what we have said of suture and powder, and what is necessary for the cure, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if he is not sound, or if the incision is not thoroughly made, because the patient cannot rest, or because of the discharge of blood, if it is recommended, fill the wound with moist cotton wool in corrosive order.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until the fat and marrow have healed, then cure it when it is sound again.</start_of_turn>
des apostemes des asselles	abscesses of boils</start_of_turn
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that arise from the buttocks are like hard carbuncles and often contain moisture.</start_of_turn>
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling that is in the abscess is emptied, if the wound is of great size, leave the cotton in place until the other side is reached, then extract all the cotton, and cure the wound that has resulted from this until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess looks like small carbuncles, if it is as we said in the incisions of carbuncles, and if the wound has burst, if necessary apply cautery as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
de la routure de l’artere	From the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin is split which is above, if there are many abscesses there as well as blood vessels escaping and bursting;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the surgeon knows well when it is for the artery, if the abscesses are long they will burst there.</start_of_turn>
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you sense it at your elbows, if you sense it, it is a dislocation; and when it is for the vein, it is a bursting of blood vessels.</start_of_turn
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover the incision with anything, and in the same way as when it is soiled with blood and pus, and when it is swollen or painful, or with a wound in the mouth or in other parts, it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, in this case, the cautery must be abandoned, and the one who is in charge must also abandon it, as in the case where an artery is burst by its bursting through the skin for a long distance
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then one must cover the size as one would with sponges, and depart the artery from the tissues, as long as it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then take a needle and pierce it through to the other side, and strain the artery with a double thread as thick as a barleycorn;  according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the arteries in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point the limb which is between the two bones of an intro-malleus as long as without loosening what is there, and cut the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then keep the wound closed while the wound edges are still bleeding;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure the wound that follows, as long as it is clean;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the wound is large enough to reach the belly, if you must hold your hand over the wound from the very start.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then hold the needle in place over the limb that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and there are two threads, so that you can pull them from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then bind the wound, as I have said, or tie one of these parts with two threads.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread does not issue from force, if it rebounds another thorn at every attempt, remove the entire thorn from the incision of the first thorn, and strain the thread in three loops.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then grasp the excess beyond what is necessary until it is spent, and then grasp the excess downwards and leave that which is joined;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a moist bandage of wine and oil, and mix together cures of bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	from abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as with an incision, comes from an artery and a vein, comes from an incision as soon as it is formed, or by too great a work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	This also happens more often with adjuvants and must do so with too much work or joint injuries, for this is what causes excessive bleeding, and its color seems like dark blood, and is in many positions causing pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is strained, if it causes pain, and is not like dark blood, but like urine;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and moves well in all parts, and does not go forward or backward, neither up nor down, and that which is in the joints cannot be closed by iron: by chance there comes contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is at the head or the chief or the front, makes the leather tough at the staple.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if he has one nail left, and grasps it at the root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is large, if the swelling has reached the bone, and scours, then cut the bone and join the wound at the suture, and cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	with great bleeding.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Never is there in the belly and never elsewhere the smell of the other, and is a disease which is called "funge" because of the resemblance of mice, and is the root subtle, and the head large; and in it are small and great peas.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw indeed at home where there were two or more bellies which resembled mice more than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had many roots, and were full of wind
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I saw indeed at home where there were two or more bellies which resembled mice more than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had many roots, and were full of wind.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the scab on the large scapula, and if you are present, perform the cautery with fire. For in this place there often comes excessive bleeding, and if it does not stop, then hasten and burn [the scab].
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient groaning and pale from the incision of the flesh, then take one thread of silk well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for three days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	Then bind [the area] and do not stop restraining the thread until the artery is completely closed, and do the work with your hand; and if the roots are loose, if there is pain in the same place for the belly, but do not push too far, cover half of it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then perform the cautery so that it does not recoil; then treat the wound and keep only the hair that is of a tawny color and poor sense and milk-stained.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a hairy swelling, and I will come to the treatment of the swelling later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is fierce.</start_of_turn
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	When the swelling appears, it comes from a burn or cut of the flesh, and is above the belly and in some there are pus, as in other parts, or blood that clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If it is by the root of the scapula and by the outlet of the bowel, if the color is like that of the abscess, it is a slight thing causing pain, and there are various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If it is by the discharge of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when it is pressed from its two sides, if it returns and comes back again, and by chance if it is tight, and causes swelling at the entrance of the bath and much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	If it is by moisture, it is a slight thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not restrain me; and if it is by blood, if it opens with these signs, the abscesses are large and hard, and are fixed in quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is by wind pressure, if the physician suspects it is due to a clot in the artery or vein, or wind pressure.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If you must leave the dressing. For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.</start_of_turn>
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if it appears to be due to the intestines or the spleen, if you command the patient to hold his breath, and be still, and sign all around the wound;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to clap his hands together.

se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it seized in the gut, if you pull it out, and stretch the intestines away from the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	If you find the bile seized, if you grasp it at the spleen, and wring out the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	If the artery opposes you, or the vein, if it will go badly into the body, then return to your work and take again.ij. needles, and there should be.ij. four strings, and hold the.ij. needles in the place where you made the incision that you thought you would make pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four days on the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the wound open until it has healed by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or thou shalt seize it when it is subtle and bear it, then cure of that which thou shalt cover, and keep the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	Then drain the blood or moisture that thou findest, then cure the wound of that which it covers, and close the wound.</start_of_turn>
dou chancre	soothe the abscess.</start_of_turn>
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the preceding chapters the signs of an abscess, and how it should be treated by medicine and how it should be cauterized; and we say that an abscess is in the marrow, and that great caution should be used in its cure, and that the old people say that when an abscess is in the bone or can be scraped out as when an abscess is in marrow, and in the hip, and similar things, and that it must be removed as soon as it begins; and when it is large and old, if it cannot be cured but must be approached, for I know of no cure for it; none have ever cured it before me.</start_of_turn>
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And in the work, when it is in place or we can remove it, as we have said, let the patient purge no more than once the black bile; then make him whole if he shows any fullness; then give him wine to make the work; then discharge his vomitings or sores, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb from your hand or from anything else, and if it comes loose from the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize too much without it being stained; then treat him of another remedy until he is healed.
de ydropisie	And in the work, when it is in place or we can remove it, as we have said, let the patient purge no more than once the black bile; then make him whole if he shows any fullness; then give him wine to make the work; then discharge his vomitings or sores, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb from your hand or from anything else, and if it comes loose from the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize too much without it being stained; then treat him of another remedy until he is healed.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	As we have said in the division, the signs of hydropathy are that the swelling is made of water, and the signs are similar to those of congestion, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only for eclipses; and one must not touch iron in these two signs: that is to say, tympanites and hydrophobia, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when medicines cause this sign of hydropathy which is called "eclipses" of medicines, and it does not profit, if you look if the patient is weak, or if there is another disease than hydropathy, as all and solution of the belly and other things; if there is no touch of iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient with great vomiting, and he has only hydropathy, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must do the work.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Believe the patient right on your hands, and the minister grasps the belly at the lower part towards the heel, then take the thumb and index finger according to this fashion: Let them be bent at a right angle at the joint, and do not allow them to go further than the intestines when you insert them, and do not pull them out.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is confined to the intestines: if you make an incision two fingers wide on the right side of the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the navel; and if it is caused by bile, make it on the right side, and do not make the patient lie on the incision that the excessive fluid does not flow to that weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the sponge, and hold your hand over the sponge between the skin and the tissue like when escorting the amount of an nail or an inch in length; then pierce the tissue as far as the sponge comes out whole, and that is the liquid, then expel the sponge, and here is the instrument: It is like a silver nail with a slight curve, and is of iron or lead, and has at the upper part a small hole; and on one side, two holes, and on the other side, one hole, and the thumb is cut off like a pen, and that is the form of the incision which the writers make with the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	The head of the arm is the support, so that when the weapon comes to the point, if it is now resting on the weapon; empty half or a third part, for if you empty more than that which can be contained in that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit of the weapon, or he will vomit, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue tell the patient, and his pulse; then draw out the weapon and hold the point, and it is held now by the thumb that is stamping the part that is above the facet, as I have said, that you pierce according to this manner; then repeat the weapon on the other side, if you see the patient suffering from that, and draw out a small quantity of liquid
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do nothing further, and take care not to use too much until it no longer stays in place. And if you doubt the patient, and you give him too much liquid, if the surgeon of the burial or sand cauterize, and by vomiting or sweating and in the sun, and take care to drink; and the surgeon of medicines that are desiccatives until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the liquid, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	From the swelling of the limb.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are children born without a perforation in the limb, or the perforation is small, or it is not firmly in its place. If you command it too soon that there is no perforation at all, even if there is much swelling according to this fashion: then put in or perforate somewhat of lead, and bind and hold it for two or three days. And when it wants to urinate, if you keep the closure closed, and make the urine, and then put it back; and by chance you cannot do anything, for the urine that comes out will not leave the closure closed.</start_of_turn>
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the perforation is small, if it is treated with a lead weight, as we have said, if it swells up. But those who do not have the perforation firmly in its place are pale, for none are born with the perforation at the head of the limb, for they cannot urinate before they raise their limb high; and they cannot urinate without this, because the material cannot come down to the marrow.</start_of_turn
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus the work must be if the patient lies prone upon his back, for the head of the shoulder and the scapula are equal in size to a thumb; if the former breaks through the middle, if as it should be; and you must hold back the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if you can staunch the bleeding of that which bleeds blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	And thus the work must be if the patient lies prone upon his back, for the head of the shoulder and the scapula are equal in size to a thumb; if the former breaks through the middle, if as it should be; and you must hold back the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if you can staunch the bleeding of that which bleeds blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these white spots in the armpit, and are an appearance of bad blood; and there are both malignant and benign ones; if it is thought that you should take them out, that is to say, ligate them secretly, and cut off their heads and roots, then put on moist cotton in Egyptian fashion; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is malignant, of a dark color and pus-filled, if you must bring in the cautery. When you have cauterized it, and if the abscess is at the root of the limb and extends partly into the nail and partly outwards, if you must break the abscess which is inside first; and when it bursts, if the cure has burst outwards. For when you cure it whole, if you do not firmly secure the limb that it is not pierced, there will be blackness and corruption in its bone and marrow; if you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour which is made of pomegranate peel and sometimes, then cure it of other cures until it is healed.

et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief. de la circoncision	De la circoncision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a matter of continuing treatment as with other wounds; however, when it is our work, we must do it with all our will, and promptly, if necessary, for our patients' well-being is more important than our reputation.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us about circumcision, for they did not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I would say that the greatest part of masters and healers who performed circumcision were fools. Indeed, there were forces and hurdles, and for all their learning, if the patient ran away because of the discomfort of the two towels, or if by chance the surgeon happened to cut too deep and left the wound open.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, and the pain is doubled, and at the loosening which is done too carelessly, the point of the limb is not firmly secured; and at the loosening of the ligament by chance escapes the spur, and repairs the work, and many times it happens that they grow without any loosening, and I desire it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	As for the loosening which is done too carelessly, I have often observed that it causes the weakening of the entire thread of hair; for the forces tear just as well from above as from below.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if you press equally from all sides, the hair will be torn; but if the hair is well stretched from the root to the skin; and if the movement of the first work makes you think of a child, if he understands, do not force him to hold the hair only by the root as little as possible, and do so for a long time;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then lay your hands straight apart, and bring the forces together between your hands or hold down your toes so that the fetus does not see them, not any instruments; then put your hand at the waist and breathe or cough, and draw up as high as the head of the fetus is engaged; then well knead the mass that is assembled there, then tie the limb with a double thread, and tie the other end to the index finger; and hold between the two threads as many as necessary, and keep the thumb relaxed and draw out the head of the fetus.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood flow out a little, and a little, for that is the medicine; and put powder on and under the powder put a bandage glued with egg yolk from a fresh hen, confirmed with rose oil and balm, and leave it on until the other side is healed, and cure again until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the juncture is like this: the two thumbs should be tense and bent, and the fingers as long as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundane if it is when the nails are forced at the incision; therefore it is fitting that you extend your nail, even though it makes an incision; and grasp it equally, and if you do not wish to keep your nail, if you hold it, and then grasp it.</p>
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they trespass two days, and that which is beside the edge is swollen, if you leave it as long as the swelling subsides, and scorch it gently; if you grasp it as you wish, and hold on to the edge of the verge, it will do you neither good nor harm.</p

dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or blood congealed, or a tumour, or worms, or similar things, as we have said in the preceding section.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the bladder or the neck of the bladder, then you must make the patient sit upright on his knees; place the thumbs outside the back, and extend the abdomen from the part below the ribs, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move as much as possible; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine will flow out freely.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If it still does not flow, and the patient experiences great pain, as we have said, then you must administer extraction with the instrument called a “syringe”; this is formed like this: either of silver or lead weight about the size of a sparrow’s quill; or of lead about the length of a thumb and a half, or of silver.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And thus the method of issuing urine is as follows: take a pair of needles, and bind one to the head of a loop of wool or cotton, and pass the needle through the syringe; then drain the excess wool and stop at the head of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and beeswax, and make the patient sit on a chair, and raise the bladder and the belly with oil moist and oily and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the syringe into the bladder, until it reaches the root of the bladder; then double the bladder downwards towards the pubic bone; then pull the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient urinate until it is empty, and this must not be done except in this order, for if it is not done in this way it will lead to a twisting; then cut the thread at both ends, and the urine will follow the thread, and withdraw it forcefully, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are bladder stones or blood in the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled, and you see urine and medicines distilling, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», and this is the shape:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it is pierced: half from one side, and half from the other, as you see; and it is grasped by the cheek so that the medicine coat is as thick as possible in the area, if we can remove the moisture, and push as much as is necessary.
