et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	And this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if it be thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if it be thus:
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round about; then strain a strong thread through these holes, and assemble the circle as though you were assembling a wheel, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture and water, and bind it up; and do as you would with a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	de la piere
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the previous section the methods of extracting stones, and the medicines used for this; and we mentioned the difference between a stone that has been embedded for a long time and one that is new, and the signs of each; and when a stone of what size must be opened in the bladder, in the uterus, and in the testicles; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is embedded in the bladder is often associated with an increase in urine, and this is a sign that the stone has burst from the bladder as if from its subtlety; and there is frequent hazing, and the patient complains of severe pain in his loin, and he urinates many times, and then becomes pale; and with these spasms the foundation is loosened; and it is light to cure the spasms until they have been going on for three years, and is more difficult in old people, and is like for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first cleanse the patient with a catharsis to drive out all the filth from the intestines. For it never hinders to explore the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the limbs, loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not rise up again; then make him sit between your hands which are placed on his thighs, and his hands are placed on his buttocks, so that the bladder is all the way down; then explore and touch inside.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hurry now to cut above the stone. And if it does not bleed at the touch, if you doubt, put your left index finger on the oil of the hand, if the patient is fat, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; and press on its foundation, explore the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, if the marrow is at the neck of the bladder; then press above your finger, and the stone will come out spontaneously or you will see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand the testicles upwards, and his left hand to grasp the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge covering, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make between the testicles and the scrotum, do not make the incision in the middle but at the cost of the left nipple; and be straight on the stone, and the two should be either close or on the foundation, and make the incision through if it is wide by pushing, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, do not make it too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the press if the stone which is or is not on the foundation, that it leaps forward in work; and sacs that there is part of the stone or it has angles, and edges: if it is grasped to stop; and if there is part which is soft, like a gland, and round, from which issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	If there are angles and margins [at the joint], make the size greater; and if it does not yield, know that you must strain above the tendons which are like a file at the head, for the bone must be strained if it does not escape; or you may use an instrument like a curved needle at the head. If you do not manage to engage it, it is wide; if it is without decor, it is the straining of vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	If there is more than one bone, strain out the greatest at the belly of the bladder first, then support above, and pull forcefully, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several. And if it is large, cover it with silk and make a greater wound. For in these things that happen to the patient: or he dies, or the urine comes to him at a greater rate than it can be held together; but whatever you do to try to drain or remove the tendons, as long as you drain them piecemeal.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe and dragon’s blood, and strain, and put upon it a wet bandage of oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up on his heel, and do not loosen the bandage until the third joint above.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have pulled it out, if there is much blood oozing from the wound, then treat with lard of olive oil and vinegar, and with lard of beeswax, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If blood clots come out of the wound and corruptions, and swelling of blood in the bladder, and whether by that the urine is retained, which is known in this part as lacking the ability to urinate without difficulty: then give him a purge in the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and bring it about.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound of water and easily and cautiously, and give him support in every way that you can, until it is healed; and cover that all the times you treat it, that you bind the wound together with sutures, and collect the medicines above the limb
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	If the stone is small, and it is either in the bladder or the urethra, and is fixed there, and the urine cannot pass; if the physician has performed what I have said above, that you should make a large incision, then you will hear of the size for this cure. I have already proved this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one fourth of an iron bar according to this form and make two angles fixed in one handle.</start_of_turn>
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the base of the stone in the bladder, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then hold the bar gently in the bladder until it reaches the stone; and turn the bar in the stone back and forth, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if the urine comes out then, press your hand on what is remaining of the stone which is in the bladder. If it is broken, and spurts out with the urine, and if there is blood, then the patient is sick.</start_of_turn
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at one end and another at the top; then bend the limb so that the bone is between the two joints, and pull it out forcefully, loosen the ligament, and massage the blood clot that is in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.</p>
de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at one end and another at the top; then bend the limb so that the bone is between the two joints, and pull it out forcefully, loosen the ligament, and massage the blood clot that is in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.</p
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is loosened in women, and this does not happen often, it is a good sign, and is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in matters of love, even among the most learned.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is that if by chance one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that if the woman’s stone is more blunt than the man’s, for in that case it can make a deeper size, and great fear has it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	If you must do this, if you can take a mistress who is well-versed, and prick her true; if you do not find one, do not cast a coarse woman; and present a woman who knows well the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of this art, and command her to do what you command of her with inquiry of the stone.</start_of_turn>
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look well if the woman is a virgin: for in that case you must push her head or foundation and inquire about the stone; and if she finds it, if you constrain her bones again, you must command her to hold her hand left on her belly, and desire and press her right hand on her belly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If it is true, when you move the testicles from the entrance of the bladder to the root of the thigh, and then press on the thigh at the root of the thigh, you will find the middle of the bone there where it is usually hidden, and you will feel the thigh in that part; do not move your hand above the thigh or below, and let the size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then tighten the wound to the size; if you feel the thigh is too tight, loosen the wound until the thigh can rest comfortably; and as for many times as you have pulled out stones, there are: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and which have much blood. If the stones resemble these, it is an indication of discharge.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not go away, if you put in a bruised vitriol and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the thigh is comfortable, and have the instruments that I have mentioned for extracting the stone be at your disposal to aid you in your work.</start_of_turn>
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go by itself, it is the artery that is cut. Put powder on the wound and hold it tight with pins and bandages. Do not attempt to move it again. Leave the wound alone and do not touch it, except in the case of an accident that causes the patient's death; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the colour of blood is calmed and the limbs are relaxed, if you return to your work, as long as the wound is open.
de hernie carnouse	of hernias of the intestines
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as dense as lead and as hard as stones, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it truly in the belly of the egg, if we take care that this is not another exercise; and it is the skin of the stone between the white fat that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramus is of weakness that comes from the stones, and is spread throughout that matter
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the stones, and this moisture has many colors: sometimes it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or pale blue, and this is more
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of a dislocation of this joint, for if it is white and smooth as we have said, if the abscess is round like the head of a fish and does not swell out, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought that it is another fish;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the smooth surface, if one feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it is of the color of the surrounding matter, thus it is like before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which comes after the introduction, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we bind them with iron, if you must, that the patient be sound according to their desire and the filling of their body; then lift them up on their back, upon something rather high, and put cloths under their knees;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on their left side, and command the minister to sit on their right side, and extend the limb towards one of the two ribs of the breastbone at the bottom of the ribs;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the towel that is left, and grasp the skin of the ribs among the bones from below the nipple, and make a straight incision dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white line, and eschew superficially according to their desire.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the face with a large hole, drain all the fluid, and then place your fingers on the face above; do not touch the root of the teeth, but only the face itself; grasp all or in pieces immediately the cost of it secretly, for if you do not grasp it well, the fluid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the liquid spurts from your work towards your eye, if you hold it in its place when you have completed the work of the face; then assemble the two parts of the teeth with a suture, and cure it as with the others wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the liquid corrupted by another disease, if you must tie the veins that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then grasp the bone throughout the suspension, drain the liquid, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the wound is assembled in two parts, their stems being two branches; if one part is grasped as the first was made even, then wipe the blood, and put linen soaked in rose oil in the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put further linen soaked in wine and oil on it, and put on the two joints, and put over doubled cloths, and bind it up in the way that is suitable for this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool like this in the semblance and assemble them by stitching in the neck of the gown, and one of the arms takes hold from the foundation up to the back, and the other from the armpit part; and the other two fingers take hold of the two angles, and everything is assembled with the restriction in the loop of the gown.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this cautery branch medicine for its size like iron; and take only a cautery with a fine point, and burn the hair, and if it is eschaufed as we have said, when the white substance which contains the fluid is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery as we have said, and prick that membrane as we have done, and burn with this fine cautery, scorched is that substance at this point.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And burn in all ways as you wish, until you have scorched it all; and keep that fire does not touch the wool; and soak that wound so that this blood will be more fluid; and keep that you are careful of excessive bleeding, and more so than in the treatment of wounds of greater size;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing else hinders you, or an abscess bursts or blood vessels burst or anything else that is contrary, if it is necessary, cure that which is contrary to it, according to what is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is weak and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if necessary, make an incision as I have said, and know for certain by the signs that we have mentioned that the wound is clean.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	If you make the patient sit up in a comfortable chair; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with a broad needle, and put the perforation through to the bone; and if the opening is large, so that all the pus comes out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the limb, and bind it, and leave only the remaining pain to flow out, then cure until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the white wool does not allow the pain to escape from the wound, as you must give her a thumb or the instrument with which the pain is treated of the hydropic, as it is formed in this way; and enlarge, that is to say, widely open the wound, and drain that the pain returns, and reassemble after about twenty days or when the pain has subsided, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will then be able to walk again.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the opening of the veins
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The wounds in this section of the limb are numerous, for it seems to me that the matter is worth leaving alone.</start_of_turn>
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that in the case of abscesses, both come from the bone, and I have seen many cases.</start_of_turn
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excess of vinegar and water, which is spread out as boils, or from percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is the color of the wound according to the color of the corn; and does not cause pain, and is grief.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance it is a wound that is greedy, foul and bloody, of dark color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.</start_of_turn>
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the position of the wound, when you press it to the side.</start_of_turn
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And you must not touch it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is made of swelling of a vein is known by his arrangement at the expression of touch of the two thumbs.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well make the size on this semblance, and on the other parts of the body.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you take hold like a leech, then the egg is up, and the thread for white silk, and release the supporter from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already swollen with these hooks, if it is to be known, that you must treat the egg and hold it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is exposed to the surface, or within the vessels, it is necessary to deliver all the surrounding fat, and round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the marrow is coming out from the bone or the heel, if you must cover it all, remove the yolk, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the work is done, if you are treating a wound, smear the wound with coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then apply other remedies until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	from the bites of the coccyx
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is a wound covered with a covering resembling a berry, with the softening of the bones.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans in pain when he moves it.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is as perilous as this one before mentioned,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and all that we say about it confirms what the ancients have said.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is fitting that you make the patient sit in a comfortable position, so that the supporter of the joints below rests against your thighs.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	Upon all the vessels that are proceeding from the groin, and grasp the master, and extend them forward;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then grasp the large scrotum at the testicles and uncover the vessels through the opening,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then pull downwards from the groin part, as we said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert a needle or if there is double thread, I tie it to the first root where the vessel has come loose, and I tie it to the other root.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then I hold the wound in the middle upright, according to the length of the limb, and I extract the corrupted moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then I treat the wound like the others or I apply a bandage, so that no vessel is cut except for those that must be cut off;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because in this way there is no harm, and if all the vessels come together, if you must cut the veins, it is better to cut them all at once;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the vein does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and if it dries up and does not swell, aid is not needed.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface of the skin
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	These events of this limb are by the section that comes or passes by the syfac, or the extension above the belly in the part of the flanks, for in this way the intestines descend from that route to one of the hips;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	These events of this limb are by the section that comes or passes by the syfac, or the extension above the belly in the part of the flanks, for in this way the intestines descend from that route to one of the hips;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the signs when it is an extension downward of the scapula, if there is little and little in the long tension, and does not come immediately;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the scapula hangs limp even toward the belly, because the scapula presses the intestines.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the scapula is fractured, that it immediately causes severe pain, and the scapula is displaced, from the stretching of the skin and the bursting of the bowels.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does the marrow go out with the intestines, and is retained as it is, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of fire with fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And thus in these cures of fire with fear, if you command or patient that he hold the bowels to his side in the wound, if it can return there;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either bind above his collar between your hands, and hold the buttocks;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the arm downwards, and press all the skin of the buttocks down long;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then from the depth of the wound, as much as the size of your hand, according to what you have learned by opening the wound, or as much as it is possible;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then pull out the hair that is under the skin, as much as the white hair of the beard is uncovered throughout;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then hold your index finger on that which lies under the beard, that which is between the white hair that is under the skin of the beard and between the second hair
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	Then pull out the hair that is under the skin, as much as the white hair of the beard is uncovered throughout; and hold the thumb of your left hand against the beard, and keep the beard against the second hair all the way up to the size of your hand;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And instruct the minister to extend the arm upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And ask if there is any intestine or white fat enclosed or hardened at the shoulder joint, and if you find nothing, grasp the belly firmly.</start_of_turn>
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or if there is thick thread made of twelve threads, and pass it through the back part of the fat, which is behind the leather of the armpits; then draw out, and cut off the ends that appear from the thread, until there are three threads left.</start_of_turn
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and bind the fat, which we have said is behind the leather of the armpits, with a strong thread of six parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then encircle the head of the shoulder with thread, and bind it firmly in three places, so that no vessel except those that nourish it can enter there, only by incision it may go.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And straighten the limb according to the first limb that is long three times as much as this one, and after these three limbs leave out the space which is between the shoulder blades like a loaf of barley that has been cut in two.</start_of_turn>
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	And afterwards according to the roundness that the eye carries; then bind in the part which is between the shoulder blades, as much as it is without pressure, and bow, as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then mix coarse wool with oil, and put it on the wound, and I mix in the thread that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is the fat cauterized beyond what we have said, after the incision, due to the fear of bloodletting.</start_of_turn>
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For often it happens that the limb swells up with blood; and if it is delayed in rising, if it is from a hot bath, put on what we have said, until it swells up.</start_of_turn
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter, I have never seen anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old people say that it is made just like the branch that joins the nut, in part like you bind the blood vessels, after the size above loosely to the dose;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put them together, and cure the abscess of what causes it, until the blood vessels groan; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Never comes routine among the angers, as we have said, and open the chest; and do not find any intestines as coils, and if there are, it is to their disadvantage, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and whenever it stays too long in that place, if one believes the wound or swelling, as long as the intestines are found;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this comes from the extension of the sinew which is in the angers, as we have said, because it is swollen, then is softened and emptied by opening the chest;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is cured by cautery, as we have mentioned before; and never by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies quite still upon his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the route enfleit downwards according to the quantity of two palms.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then draw out the scab which is beside the leather that covers it, then take hold of the root and bring the limb appearing from the scab outwards.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press on the front of the belly, then cut the two thumbs appearing from the scab on the top of the root, and cut one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then draw out the root, and do not cover the scab or extend the gut or anything else, as I told you in the cure of the root of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat the wound by the treatment of wounds. And when you have closed the wound, if the wound bursts and heals the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The surface is contracted, and shows no mark in the course of treatment, and the cautery is useless in this location, and the surrounding parts are more susceptible to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the nails of the house are softened in lukewarm water, for the nails that are within are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to scrape off the softened leather on the natural leather; then assemble the layers one over the other with a seam, and if you see that, close the first excess of softened leather with two or three stitches firmly; then scrape between the stitches and cure as the other wounds, until they are healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	When the limb is chastened
des hermofrodites	Saiches that chastening is commanded in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary to do so for two reasons: the first is that the patient will respond when asked in the saige; and the second, because we have often had to cauterise beasts for our attendants, as with oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts. I say therefore that chastening is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.  In the one that we do by traction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the hairs are softened and pliant; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are set and you no longer feel them.  Of the size of the chastening: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the hairs with your left hand, then bind the suspenders, and grasp each heel with one hand, as when you have well supported them; and leave no wound or any secret wound that is outside the vessels; and this method of chastening is milder than that which is done by traction, because at traction remains by chance no part of the hairs, by which the beast desires to loosen.  Then cure the wound until it is healed.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as in homes: one if between the two testicles opens as with the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the court it urinates. And the other manner if it is in women, and has upon the navel as a beard and two testicles. And the cure of the womb and fame if it is that you cut out all the seminal vessels, and the cure if like other wounds; in the second manner, of homes whose urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a seminal vesicle upon the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand. And the cure is this. It is necessary to hold the excess of the tenticle at your hand or as desired; and do not go too deeply, for from there blood does not come; then cure from another cure until it is healed; and there is another thing that comes from the mouth of the marrow, and the emptying, and by chance leaps out, and is like a bladder, and for this reason it is called the ancient "madness of the kidney". If it is possible to cut it out, as we have said the tenticle, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	If the nature of the woman is not clearly discerned, or the opening is small; and if it is natural by birth, or an accident from disease that has come to be; or by a char of garlic, or a soft or thick syfat, and is made by pushing in the armpit, or in the breast, or on the genitals, or otherwise; and if it is suspected that there is an embolism nearby, if there is pain in the two thighs or the groin. If there is a soft syfat and it is nearby, and if there are two levers, if you hurry, and pull them together: put your two thumbs together, and let the woman be on her back, spread her legs; then the two levers will form, as long as the soft syfat is round, and let it go over the embolism; then take hold of the limb, and anoint it with oil, and put it on the limb, and let the woman lie down comfortably, if it cannot be healed. And if the syfat is hard and thick, if you must cut it with a scalpel resembling a berry leaf. If the embolism is of a nail, if you suspend it on the navel and cut it off; have the medicines that stop bleeding, such as acaice, dragon’s blood, incense, together with many eggs; then mix in a large dose of lead. Let the wound be long, and mix in a string of linen; and let it be cured of other cures until it is healed. And if in the armpit comes a nail, if you cover it according to this manner, this will prevent infection. For infection is what is in the armpit, do not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of emboli.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually happen; and when they are old, they become tough. As we have said before in the division, the signs and symptoms are these which announce healing. I say that emboldened veins and those which are full in the marrow do not feel pain, except when they are cured by fire. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the thumb and hold the index finger at its root, then sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragons blood, and incense, and the like; then close her up an hour later, and put her in cold water; and if there is any remaining blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and the like, and then drink barley flour, and mix it with honey and anise, and make a paste of it. And if it has clotted, that is good. If not, make her cough up phlegm at the back and put on a plaster. Then take linen and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her cough up. And when the abscess is quiet, if it is cured, the limb will regain its natural position as long as it is healthy; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a severe wound, if you cover it as I have said the tough one; and then it will be cured as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually happen; and when they are old, they become tough. I say that emboldened veins and those which are full in the marrow do not feel pain, except when they are cured by fire. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. And if it has clotted, that is good. If not, make her cough up phlegm at the back and put on a plaster. Then take linen and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her cough up. Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Emoroids are openings of veins which usually happen without restraint, but when they become old, they harden. As we have previously mentioned in this section, the signs and symptoms that suggest healing are these. I say that emboldened veins and those which are full in the marrow do not feel pain, except when cured by fire. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow we can feel, and these are the ones we can cure. Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, extend the thumb and hold the index finger at its root, sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragons blood, and incense, and the like. Close her up an hour later and put her in cold water. If there is any remaining blood, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry, and drink barley flour mixed with honey and anise. If it has clotted, that is good. If not, make her cough up phlegm at the back and apply a plaster. When the abscess is quiet and cured, the limb will naturally regain its position. The one that is called "albathir" is red and resembles a severe wound. If you cover it as I have mentioned, it will be cured.
de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The master first teaches at the play that she knows the figure of the natural birth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down on the jaw, and desire to smell the breast: then the child comes out with force; so his limbs that are naturally born according to the figure are born with the head down, and comes out head first, and is accompanied by it; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on his belly, if the child comes out head first, he is delivered; for when he descends upon his head, he is accompanied by it, and the mother delivers the afterbirth by natural force; and this is not in any way natural. For it does not come once from its parts, but comes from force of the womb or the uterus, or the hands, or it comes from its belly, or even from behind, and is converted by an accident from its collar, and by other harmful figures; if the master is at the play that she is wise and discreet in these matters, and avoids error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures that we must help her with.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out head first by natural birth, and the woman is groaning, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and arise her nature from oil or rue or fennel seed, and then bring her between her two legs the little cushion from which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment. et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and I apply plasters, soak in soft and moist water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on his side, put him even, if he remembers what we said about the living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if he does not remember, if he cries out involuntarily, do not leave anything of the afterbirth behind.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if he remembers what we have said about afterbirth, as it comes in the belly.</start_of_turn
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if there is discharge of blood comes, if there is any restraining water, and other cures are administered.</start_of_turn
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom a child was born dead, then consulted with another concerning it, and refuted death in the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came a swelling in the belly, and it burst open, and began to swell greatly.</start_of_turn>
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went for help, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the bleeding.</start_of_turn>
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong compresses, and out came a bone, and after a few days another.</start_of_turn
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at mouth, for this belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I wish for the wound, and in treating hands bones, as long as the woman was improving;

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of the pressure, which is to keep the book closed; and there are two returns as two fingers of two hands.

et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the mouth be wide open, i.e. two fingers wide, and the tongue must be drawn out, and as long as a palm and a half.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And in between let the two limbs be two fists wide apart, which are closed together, half a palm long or more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two fist-closures are held in the mouth of the patient when the corners are turned over
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And he has twice struck his joints twice at the shoulder, as you see, from a wound that is long and wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	And when you see the wound opening up all around the instrument, if you make the woman sit with her head resting, keep the feet still and the legs over

puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then cover your hand over the instrument as much as you see the wound opening up in the mouth of the wound, until the pain ceases.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very sharp, and their resemblance multiplies their danger; and when you behold them appear, the work hastens, and the higher you are in your home the greater is your quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not covet the instrument when you do not see it, for its necessity is not to be excused
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to retain its limb, and then make it cough out of condition, and strain your hands to the mouth and neck;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it leaps out for that, well is that.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take one pot and make a hole or incision, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as chamomile, rue, anis, camomile, cassia and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, whether cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a sponge or incision in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marrow.

Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	If the second joint remains after this treatment, and is not better, as it is commanded at the dance, she must moisten her left hand with oil of poppies or with alum, and then put it back in its place.</start_of_turn>

mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but must move gently forward and backward, and then treat; for if it comes and disappears.

If it is deemed necessary, then appropriate fumigations are useful in this case: neither of the ancients have proven the effectiveness of fumigation with rosemary and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at the retention of urine and the secondine if it is necessary is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like a cane, and we put the handle over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	Or let the fumigations be over the charcoal, and the brim until it is consumed, and begin again.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Whoever pierces the foundation does not give birth to children who have not fully grasped its support, but has stifled them with a subtle snare.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, if one must pierce that snare, do not pierce it cruelly with a pointed instrument, but hold the lacement so that it does not touch;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on coarse cloth soaked in wine and oil, and the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, put or draw in a weight of lead, and leave hands clasped, and be still until the swelling subsides.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Never again will this wound or abscess come to mind; if it covers itself: if it is cured, as we have said concerning the weight of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation.</start_of_turn>
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodular and grow greater when they come from the base of the foundation, or between the two parts,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is a fistula or several; and when that swelling is old, if it persists, and is accompanied by moisture which causes a white or bluish swelling,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	They never stay put; and are known by the fact that they occur when there is discharge or wind pressure when the patient evacuates, and by chance when one leaps forward.</start_of_turn>
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half of the thigh; and reach up to the joint of the hip, and up to the navel.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the permanent fistula from the transient.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bite your thumb or foundation, and insert a subtle needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is swelling, if you insert a slight attempt of sponge, or hair, as long as you feel the attempt or hair on your thumb;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of blood or wind or swelling, as we have said.
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	it is not pierced; if you hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is formed up to the bladder or the urethra, if in leaping the urine escapes and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is seen up to the hip joint, if there is a vein running up to the limb;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the limb is not bent, if it is only slightly bowed, and no medicine or ointment will help;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistulas formed up to the bladder there is no other cure than toil, and the vanity of fools who interfere with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is neither new nor old, hope for health with fire, as I have seen.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and keep the legs stretched out as far as his thighs, and let his thighs lean towards his belly
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then make an attempt to stretch, or press if there is stiffness, until you can see or feel that it is relieved.

se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	He feels that he has perceived it; and whether it is discovered or you feel between your shoulder blade and your chest, then the wound that is perceived.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not slip away with it, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	We can do everything well enough to heal it, but that does not always happen;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and if we do it cautiously, according to the size of the fistula, as it is said;
