et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then treat the soft scabs with burning, until these hairs vanish; then treat the wound with ointment, applying pressure and closing the wound.</start_of_turn>
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is well closed, that is good. But if not, it cannot be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule à ce qui enseut la coverture dou keur.

Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he will not move, and the surgeon is between him and the work, if the fire cautery or the medicine is hot.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together three bones: namely, the burning of these cartilages, the evacuation of blood and the drying out of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the cure of soft tissues, burned or cut into pieces, until the bones crack and the cartilages burn in the wound;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then cure the wound of the sores with dry powder, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula arises up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the bone or root is grasped or questioned concerning this.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the attempt, and there is blood or pus, or a tumor, or it is near piercing, if there is no other way out but hope, by the administration of one of these three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	you cauterize as we have said, or you drain it until it is empty, or if you wish, you may try and cure it from the beginning.</start_of_turn
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too quickly, for you must cover the dwelling that holds the foundation, and come out in the direction of the will; otherwise you will cause ejections.

si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a perceived attempt at the head like this:

des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Emorrydes are of two kinds: either they are deep-seated, like grains of sand, and are small and large in number, or they are close to the surface of the skin without breaking through it.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if there is one or more of them, they are displaced from the socket and from the root of the bone; but those that are displaced often have moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and are often accompanied by bleeding or a yellow or bloody discharge, and have a pale color.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the cure for these things that are within the foundation, if you command the patient to groan and rise up to his chamber, as long as the foundations are firm, and it will become clear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and grasp it with your nails, or hold it with your finger, then grasp it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if it slips from your grasp due to moisture, if you take hold of it with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chammock cloth.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and draw it towards your shoulders, then grasp it, and powder over it hot powder that are in lieu of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or thou causest them to cauterize as it is said or as in the treatise of cautery, and then heal them of other remedies while they are whole;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot withstand, if you bite the patient with biting and rough tweezers to uncover what is or is under the foundation, if it can be loosened openly.</start_of_turn>
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	cannot the patients endure, and if the strings are too tight for the foundation, if it is the gentle cure;  </start_of_turn
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and take them at your nail or with forceps, and hold them, then cure them as we have said, while they are whole, and make the incision with iron to stop the bleeding.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you consent that you will follow this manner: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through from below and draw out the needle from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread around the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	If it is large; tighten the thread further, then knot the thread, and draw out the needle, and make sure to secure all the others, leaving one to correct the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put upon the foundation one moist bandage in rose oil or beeswax, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it until it shrinks, and when it has shrunk, if the treatment of oil and other remedies, while sane.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when it is dry or firm.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is advanced and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you can, rest at the point of a scab or at your nail the crust underneath, which does not let it moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then treat it until it is healed as much as it can;  if it is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be calmed, if you must repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it is numb, and be escorted;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed
dou fremit	completely.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice est une petite apparance fautrée antor le corps, et va mout em parfont.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small appearance that appears before the body, and goes through without leaving a mark; and never is its touch perceived, and it is felt as if death is near, and comes throughout the body, and more is found in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a sponge of a hen’s quill, or a quill of strong vulture, and put that sponge on the wound, until the blood circle encompasses the wound all around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then tighten your hand with all the sponge so that you can encompass the wound all around, and put it through, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that he does this with a needle or iron as it is said above, and be subtle and restrain his limbs:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see that he does this with a needle or iron as it is said above, and be subtle and restrain his limbs, do not make it obvious, for it must be kept secret, and press firmly. de la forme dou clistere	de the form of a blister.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a blister with silver or gold, or with melted lead or mercury; and never make a blister with these small and large instruments, as they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in their children and infants are puny.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is excessive, or the belly is tied up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and if there is a swelling or the belly is tied up, as you see, and the limb is pierced through or split open; there is a hole on one side, or on the other side.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	or the belly is filled with the best medicine or parchment, and the hole is pierced all around the wound
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And between each part there must be space, then stretch these parts apart with a strong thread of strong thread twisted in a cross or hooked at one end, and assemble the belly as if it were a nail.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	When the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument before a strong thread, then clinch; and this is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	Neither too hot nor too cold, and join the head of the clinch with oil or balm of egg, or something similar, and hold it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then grasp the minister with his two hands assembled, until it is completely visible, then withdraw the clinch, and leave the patient his legs at rest,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	If the physician sees that the limb is still painful, if he can tolerate it, and if he sleeps all night without pain; this is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he has put it on in a state of sickness of swelling of the belly, and the physician wishes to depart, if he begins as soon as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	If there are pus or swelling, or an abscess, if the swelling is as subtle as that of a child;  </start_of_turn
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is the form of the subtle swelling on which the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the previous chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather, the treatment of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what causes them, and depending on the limbs or parts of the body that are wounded, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things that cause wounds are by the bite of a stone, and the size of a spear or nail, or of a lance or fist or stone, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or that which is done according to the laws of the cure, if like wound that bites upon the neck, or upon the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, or other limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Or that which is done according to the laws of the cure, if like wound that bites upon the neck, or upon the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, or other limbs. And I shall tell you of the cure for simple wounds, for the memory of it will come back to you in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or chief, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is not from a stone or other things, and the skin is completely ruptured and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And you doubt the wound's depth: if you do it too cautiously, the head of the casualty himself will suffer from the blood of the wound; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the limb.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen to the patient's swelling of wine and meat
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	and if he does not see better, if he is fed meat, do not drink wine, do not eat cheese;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put out the wound, if it is festering, soak in oil of roses only, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	If there is no oozing from the wound, if you put a dressing on it when it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, I shall tell you about it later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood has been moved, put on some ointment until it has healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a nail and some, and the layers do not gather together by tension, if you gather them together by stitches, as I shall say for wounds in the belly, of stitching
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered of bone, and is open, and can only be held together by a thread, if you can; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hair instead of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat plenty of solid foods, such as testicles and wheat bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or see putrescence on the skin, and it does not touch the bone, if you bite down firmly, and lick the wound, then cure it.</start_of_turn>
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched by medicine, if you can tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.</start_of_turn
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does not help, cauterize it.</start_of_turn>
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a minor cure: then put on this powder which solidifies as soon as it has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; and chalk three parts, and grind the powder finely.</start_of_turn>
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and hold it firm, until it is well aired and unites with all its blood.</start_of_turn>
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it firmly, and let it drain, if it does not swell; for we do not keep the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we do this chalice solely, when we have neither incense nor blood of dragons, but only when the wound has not moved.

de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If this is the case, if there is no other remedy except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restrictive, for it is night and it makes the wound retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the night is cold, and its continuation is with the marrow, which is the strongest member.</start_of_turn>

et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.</start_of_turn

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of a lance or a knife</start_of_turn

dou derrompement dou ventre	Pain of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The pain of the belly is great, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	The great wound does not leave the intestines at any time, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the presence of worms;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the large wound is more painful than the small wound ever is.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of this it is more proper to point the intestines in and out again rather than to leave them exposed.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Forasmuch the intestines swell greatly that they feel the fruit, if they return inwards more by points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	Because the intestines swell greatly that they feel the fruit, if they return inwards more by points, it is worth noting that the spleen may be injured, for because of this we must keep the intestine in its place like others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And the wounds that arise from the rupture of the belly are in three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the three common sutures appear in the belly suture,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	And the stitching of other wounds with silk and thread is common as other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all of them are more pure with the stitching of the belly, and I shall speak a little and declare.</start_of_turn>
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no gut thing inside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if anything is grasped, this is in two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	Or for the slightness of the wound, as we have said.
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Or because the intestines are swollen with the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, evacuate the vomit in parts sparingly:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wet a sponge or rather a cloth in cold water only,

et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, if there is an opening in the wound at the instrument, we grasp the hemorrhoids there.</start_of_turn>
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is mute as the size,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	because there is no need to cut with great necessity nor to go too far.</start_of_turn
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for cutting.
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut downwards in the curve and do not veer off, and once you have made this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	and when the wound is swollen, and the intestines are forced out,

Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and is in the lower part of the belly,

et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus it is proper to administer that which I have said concerning great and painful wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds do not require such measures
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then hold your hands apart, that is, administer with great care, which will keep all the blood vessels open
et assemble les levres;	and close the wounds.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	And this is the common method of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound's size,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave some of the wound's chief, i.e. space, and pierce a needle or there is good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two holes in the leather with the two holes in the silk,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	Who is so sore as to pierce the skin of that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	Who is so sore as to pierce the skin of that part,
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	and brings together the three heads of the shoulder together.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the three heads of the limb that are coming forward,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then leave some space and insert another hook.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then leave some space and insert another hook. Then hold the thread as you did for the first hook.</start_of_turn>
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this until you have made several hooks.</start_of_turn
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wounds are restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	And be the needles blunt, between marrow and bone,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the blunt needles pierce all the marrow, and the too great if they do not penetrate me well to enter:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because it is proper that they be blunt;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and must not pierce too deeply into the marrow or skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	They do not hold and open the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	Then close the holes of the arrows, so that they do not bleed the patient at night,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and put patches or cloths over the holes of the arrows to hold them in place,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	And this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because there is often a needle or two involved.</start_of_turn>
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common.</start_of_turn
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and that you assemble the hair of the leather and the hair of the silk together with a needle or there is much fine thread in between;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	And when you have perceived these things all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if you remain calm at the part where you began, in this way you will keep the spasms in check.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place between each suture the thickness of a small hazelnut;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture will be sufficient for the home,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	And I sutured a wound thus when one had a wound on the hip or belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was caused by a knife.</start_of_turn>
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and was more than a palm wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was filled with blood to the amount of two palms.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And it was the wound in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	Then I brought back the intestine when it had been out for twenty-three hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was closed after fifteen days, and the patient was healed, and was well again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they marveled that he had died, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I will not fear the washing, for I am in a place where one does not go, neither with medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And thus more sense is made upon the wound seven times a day, and the washing of honey until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or you will say the two right ways of dressing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pass it through from the lower part up to the part inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When she has perceived the right shoulder in the right place, if the head hangs limp or is stiff or the hook has been pulled out,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and makes her perceive from the other side of the limb up to this very moment.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and understands this matter as well as a tailor does the hair
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leaves one side of the shoulder, and takes it back from the other, until the dislocation is completely healed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, as Galen often does,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is like this with no other, which assemble the two parts naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and join one chief to the other cheek, in a partial manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or hook nearby, and make the latter slip only,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	et laisse les poils dou syfac.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then prick at their base, and hold the eyes steady until they grow to the root,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as hair on the face;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then prick at their base, and hold the eyes steady until they grow to the root, as hair on the face; then prick the one and the other from the lower part until they reach the root, with other hair between them.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most frequent and usual method of treatment.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	If this word is repeated, and no one testifies to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	we must suture the belly with nine or ten needles, or there must be thread in the wound;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and we must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and the arrows that when they are withdrawn from the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and the arrows that when they are withdrawn from the belly, if the wound is deeper than usual, the pain is greater.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though it has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	If you reset the intestines and the pain persists; then put on a coat of char-pulverizing powder.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	If the pain persists even after resetting the intestines; then put on no other dressing except what is necessary, until the wound is healed.</start_of_turn>
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	Close the wound, and keep the dressing in place, and observe;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure the wound like any other until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you have no medicine, if you put it on, as soon as it begins to swell, cotton wool,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And if you have no medicine, if you put it on, as soon as it begins to swell, cotton wool,
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For there is no need of other medicine in many cases where wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not spread to the principal parts,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	If it is certain that you moisten coarse linen cloth in hot oil of poppy or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put them on the boils, and anoint the sores.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	if there is pain or decay in the bones, and it happens often,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the clusters of black wine swell up and the marrow comes down to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And the spleen, and the intestines, if they are large, are lighter to cure than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The large intestine which is called the "jeun" cannot be cured when it is swollen
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	because of the swelling of the veins and the delicacy of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	if it be spurted from the wound, if it is returned behind as soon as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	If it is dark and becomes black or blue, know that you must bind the black limb, for no blood flows there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	and bind what is between the limb,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the joints loose from the lower part of the wound until it is displaced when the bone is cut, and the wound is healed.
de la routure dou boueil	From the root of the bone.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if its position is restored in its natural place,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that one bone was fractured or belly of a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	And it was the wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became filled with pus, and in this there was vomiting and diarrhea.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put it to cure according to what I could, and did not cease until it was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closed, I doubted that the patient would be well in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And there is no harm, but remains in many arrangements, meals and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And the physicians say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligated in a timely manner.
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	having taken great precautions, and then unite the layers of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the bleeding has ceased, if you put on the skin the two layers,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	If her tongue is strained above;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then she holds the head still, and this remains if it cannot be loosened.</start_of_turn>
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another bandage afterwards in this way as before, until the wound is completely healed.</start_of_turn>
et cout la plaie.	and bind the wound.</start_of_turn>
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated in the intestine, and causes no discomfort to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated in the intestine, and causes no discomfort to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread which is cut from another intestine.
en teil maniere:	thus.
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	and take the head of this thread of intestine which is freed from its discharge,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	And then bind the chief of this thread, namely a thread of fine linen, taut.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then pass the thread through the needle, and through the intestine, and hold it in place in its path;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching is not fierce but according to the way of the vein and the expectation;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even if it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no other remedy, save only by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	From fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	When it covers all wounds or incisions, whenever it breaks open, it is called a fistula universally.</start_of_turn>
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it is closed and returns inwards.</start_of_turn
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	and fistula is according to truth a nodulation that must be hard and white, or where there is no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it is just like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	never straight in clear water, and sometimes spread out.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never quite, and sometimes quite widely.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	that every wound that is not cleansed will have its discharge, and there is no pain that does not leave its mark.
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	This is not fire but by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or bone;
ou por sa malice;	or by its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or by the violence of movements, or because of the hardness of some substance within, and upon the limbs, which prevents new growth.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or il i a trop de bowe;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or there is too much bow; or the limb is protruded, and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the cure.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is rampant like pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	Or for the property in the region is late the digestion, and late the health, and flees by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	Or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already mentioned these causes, the signs, and the cures of medicines in this division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I will tell you the cure of fistula which is made by the sweat of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Hair that has become fistulated appears in all limbs with pain.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or at the spleen, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the bones,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the shoulder blade, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if part comes to the property of the principal limb, and there remain some of them.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that does not come out except just as I have said, and you have promised a cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see that it is known, if you take an attempt to drain or burn it, if the fistula is straight, if the wound is cured;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	If the fistula bursts, if a cunning worm attempts to plunge,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the worm plunges into the cavity of the fistula.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has holes and you cannot close it well with sutures,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the bladder is burst by one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For the moisture is so strong from a pierce to another, and the earth is made firm.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then when its weight rests on your belly, you must know if there are bones or nerves, and that it is firmly supported,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the limb or its place, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	Or in other cases which I have mentioned, if the limb conforms to what I have said,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and the bones are stiff and corrupted that are within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the cure must be completed when it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well deep from the right side, if you must pierce through, as much as you wish,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	Then I put soft compresses in medicine of the fistula, and I keep them until the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine softens the excess that is dissolved at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put greasy substances on the wound, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it does not heal by this, if we must cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupted from a fistula, take hold of it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the belly or nerves are not grasped or the principal limbs, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is discovered, and there is corruption and blackness, if the limb remains as long as the corruption is complete,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure for such things as are dangerous until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	If he is not healed, and if he returns home like before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	if he is not cured, and if he goes home like before, he will certainly return again soon.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if he persists in his sickness and stays at home just as before,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and restore the limb;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is still sound, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	And if that is not the case, know that corruption has spread too far, and there is no use in proceeding further;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	unless there is some other remedy save leaving things to their own course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	or if there is a slight fracture, and you try to mend it with pins and needles,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	If the extraction is made with a suitable instrument, it covers that which is convenient.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	If there is any remaining bone, if the thread is torn, do not leave it there;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	if moisture opposes you, and there is no doubt or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if bone and moisture and hair are together, and the bone is freed.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you do not remove them at an hour, if you put something upon the wound that encourages corruption,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	leave them so long as the bones are exposed.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will be more easily fractured.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	it is important that you do not move them.
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	If the patient feels such great suffering as to cause the corruption to swell as much as the marrow is white,
puis restoure la plaie;	Then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of the corruption, and it comes up to the marrow bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then cover it with a bandage and cover all until the corruption is healed; and then cure it until it is healed completely.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I will tell you of a fistula that had its origin in the home of her leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take this as an example and assist in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was once a young man about .xxx. years of age, who had a pain in his leg caused by something within the bone,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg, and there was a large abscess, and no cause was found by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	But the marrow thereupon bursts so much above as the abscess bursts.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and from there bursts out mouthfuls of matter, and becomes a fistula, and there comes out mouthfuls of pus that all clot and moisture with blood.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and remain for a year and a half, and there is no wise man in the art of healing,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	since I was called here, and saw the limb and the medicines which were being used.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And that which is cured by the wounds has great pain;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And becomes red like blood the body of a young person, and had the color of citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I bound a loop in one of these wounds, and then circled all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one vein followed the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and grasped in one of the holes until I discovered a piece of bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it fractured and perceived it, and knew its decay went right down to the bone itself.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to me a fractured bone, and I thought that there was no other decay except for that which I saw;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with various medicines so long as I could, but could not mend it.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then I repeated the procedure, and I discovered the bone as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And I found the disease continuing in the bone, the marrow, and the blood vessels, and I considered soldering the bone together
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I was unable to do so until I had fractured a part of the bone, and the marrow burst out completely.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored the remedies; and he was healed and restored to health immediately.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And he will no longer dare to renew the work because of the patient’s weakness, who cannot endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for fear of death which I fear for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often there is the evacuation of blood, but he remained entirely well,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and he produced in his place a hard bone, and was of good disposition and did not suffer any discomfort or anything contrary to all, neither fear nor coming to an end
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is fractured in no place except for pain, if it is recommended to bandage it in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one thread, and strain it at the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	command no one to stretch it up high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another thread of linen thicker than the first one on the skin that is outside the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And thus is the head displaced, if you draw the corrupt marrow from the socket.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the marrow above the bone or you see silk there, that the silk does not stain the marrow;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a swab or a towel of lead over the bone to cover the corrupt marrow;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and cover so much silk as one can see and feel the corruption, and cover again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open wide, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the whole limb; then put one stone weight on it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then stretch from one end to the other the corruption, and keep it stretched for a space as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint, and stretch the bone or the part which contains the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is continuous in the neighborhood of these two joints, if there is no other vessel except the vein of the groin.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is at the root of the arm or the thigh, if it is strong in this matter
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but in any case you must inquire about the cause of that dislocation, how it happened to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and be mindful of all means, but that the vein or nerve does not impede you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And the nails which he incisions and the threads which cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of swellings.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their thinness, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;

et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and the nails which he incisions and the threads which cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of swellings.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the testimony of the manners of diseases;

Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated that corrosion with the remedies of medicine, but it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if it is necessary to cover that limb up to the root or the corrosion recurs.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by that of death, or by malice, which is greater, the defect of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And thus after the dark, then comes that corruption of limb against limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And thus after the dark, then comes that corruption of limb against limb,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and seizes throughout the body; if you are hasty in your covering,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	and if there is percussion from venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea, vipers and similar beasts, if the head is struck, and you do not give it space to move until the hand arrives.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the wrist, if the bone at the joint is fractured, so that the decay does not reach the forearm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes up to the arm, if the bone at the shoulder is fractured, so that the decay does not reach the upper arm.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and only then will there be no other remedy than the strength of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and whatever you do, when the corrosion comes or is delayed: if it comes to the first joint, if the bone afterwards reaches the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or if it is urgent, grasp all the urgency;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it rises to the limb, if you grasp at the joint of the elbow.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the elbow, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient dead;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the patient’s limb if you bind it below and above,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And extend one minister from the lower lip, and another minister from the upper lip,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you shall split the lip that is between the two lips with one inch of space, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cover it with pitch or silk, and put one bandage of linen under the lip so that the silk does not touch the sound tissue.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and come to the patient other wound and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the limb urgently,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is accompanied.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb securely with a strong bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there is a home for you here.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackening that seemed to burn with fire.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption first arose in his armpit, so that it blackened the whole limb.</start_of_turn>
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when we saw the corruption, if we covered the limb, it healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that it returned, the corruption or the shoulder, and I came to him,

et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it bursts and breaks through, and in leaping out, it breaks the bone, and it remains broken.</start_of_turn
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin which is under is just as subtle as a silken drape that is unrolled.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula".

et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, if you burn with fire, and then cover the vein from the shoulder to the elbow, or in the lower part at the ankle;

et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And hold that it does not touch, for if it touches, if it cannot be moved or raised, there results in harm to the patient.

De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the leg, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it happens outside the leg; this comes from corruption that comes from the decay of the leather.

puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limb is changed, and the vein starts to swell, like the root of a plant.

por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and thoroughly, and that nothing remain or be left behind.</start_of_turn>

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From the navel to the heel between leather and hair.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This ailment is called in our land "beef disease", because it often happens after bouts of eating.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	it is a small swelling that arises between skin and bone, and spreads throughout the body, ascending and descending
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and causes great pain in all the limbs, as long as the skin or the bone is pressed, or if it bursts
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	it is caused by the inflammation of certain humors, such as veins, arteries, and blood clots or worms and tumors
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And doubt arises of its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	And indeed it returns by chance, and destroys the oil; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if you cannot drive it out until it is gone:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must certainly bind the limb above and below with a strong and well-stitched ligature,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then grasp above and forward, and if the limb is grasped too tightly in the chair, you will not find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery is done above, as long as it burns;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm it makes is when it runs into the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, grasp above and forward, and grasp tightly

et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And warn him of eating rotten meat
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land “vakirir,” and is a pain that comes in the limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And thus, if it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen that which I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I went to see a sick woman, and found her arm swollen at the elbow;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and as I looked afterwards, I saw that the swelling had gone up like a worm to the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more swollen than anything, like gold that has been cut in two;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that limb and spreads to the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then afterwards it turns crooked throughout the limb, until it reaches the opposite arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and I heard that it twisted back towards the limb, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel how it moves from limb to limb, because I have never known of such a disease like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Whatever, I advise that if you wish to keep me, do not move your limb with pain towards another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not wish that, as if I saw it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this was because the women had dry skin and the veins uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appeared that constraint of the wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not depart from me according to this reason for those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and veins filled with blood.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	When you see that this illness is cured, and the patient feels the pain as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the liquid above and below has become stagnant, and then swells up as much as that constraint of the wind opposes.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the physician who dispenses these anti-inflammatory remedies, like foul pills and pilules of serapin, and similar things.
Des saiettes	If the physician who dispenses these anti-inflammatory remedies, like foul pills and pilules of serapin, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	If the physician who dispenses these anti-inflammatory remedies, like foul pills and pilules of serapin, and similar things.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	If the physician who dispenses these anti-inflammatory remedies, like foul pills and pilules of serapin, and similar things
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those which have two joints, and those which have tongues, and those where there are fragments; and that which tears in no limb tears in two ways: either in the main limb it tears,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the forearm it tears. In the heel, the elbow, the shoulder, the hand, the foot, the intestine, the bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it tears in no limb of these limbs, and the sign of death is shown, which I will tell you later, you will learn:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you suspect that the extraction of this arrow will cause damage, for indeed the blood comes afterwards in various positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	If it is clear that the sign is bad and you do not perceive the arrow to be deeply embedded, if you hesitate, cure the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	The sign of the fracture is that the arrow pierces the bone, and leaps up the substance which is above the brain.</start_of_turn
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	This is when the body is cut, soaked in sweat and vomit, with pain in the belly, vomiting of bile; inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and loss of consciousness, and vomiting of the bowels.</start_of_turn>
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And by chance it is without force of noses, or ears; and by chance it takes away speech and voice.
