Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the splinter when it hurts or swells, is that it is near the left breast, and feels as though it were fixed in something hard, do not break it open;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the scapula moves like the nails, in dark blood, and comes cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	There is doubt that death approaches.</start_of_turn>
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the scapula which never departs from the wound is that there is no swelling of the wound, the throat swells, the patient’s face turns pale, and he sighs loudly and stops eating.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the scapula breaks through the covering of the pit, if there are little bones there; there is great pain, great swelling and great pain, and he sighs; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the spleen or stomach bursts open by chance, nothing of the indigestible meat escapes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the spleen or stomach bursts open by chance, and by leaping out of the intestines nothing escapes from the wound, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the spleen.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the spleen bursts open in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out in flow, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.</start_of_turn>
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if like the face and the throat and the chest and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine and the backbone and the thigh and the calf and the ankle, the limb mentioned above is subject to many conditions.</start_of_turn
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this the patient makes another thing.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	When the splinter is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this the patient makes another thing. There was once a splinter which slipped or drooled at the root of the tooth:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to grasp it, and drew it out from the grease of the ear, and it was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And drew out a splinter that had slipped into the grease of the oil from the ear of a peasant.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was settled, and it did not reach anything except the tip towards the flank.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And it was an arrow from a Turkish bow, quite light in weight; the wound was clean, and there were no bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And carried an arrow from the throat to a crest, and the Arabic arrow had an ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I saw the beards, and endured until I carried it, and was saved from the crest.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he shot an arrow at home, that was in the thigh or belly, and thought he was dying.
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that he did not pass thirty days, if he did not mend his way;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut off the arrow, and bound it, and pulled out the shaft, and there was no further mishap.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if a man at home had an arrow go through or back, and the wound was deep above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And immediately he removes the bandage from within, and does not change his natural inclinations.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	he finds no satisfaction in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And thus another man, to whom he applied a bandage to his face, was healed of his wound;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and immediately he suffered great pain; and many others suffered like him.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And carried out an arrow at once from among the princes of the king, who was sitting close to them all.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was leaning to the right side; and the arrow was fully retrieved.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I went to see the patient after two days. If I found the wound much more swollen.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I put it under a slight tension, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt no tingling or pain from his ear to his jaw.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of an arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on a protective plaster bandage so that it would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and he appeared to me to be the tip of an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I place the thumbs at the joints, and restore the wound to its proper place, and maintain the patient’s hand long tense.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he feels the splinter [arrow] still inside his wound; and he tells me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I place above the wound corrosive medicine with my thumbs, until it is well over,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I touch it and feel the head of the arrow which is coming out;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I assisted in the opening of the wound by that cunning physician, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and stayed there for three months altogether.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I enlarged the wound so that I could insert the nails, and the two parts together, and I could not bear it
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I continued to toil and devise various methods using instruments, until I finally obtained a pair of nails well made,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what is said at the end of this chapter, as long as I remain here, I will treat the wound and restore it.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And it is judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or as you have said the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you place your treatment upon that which I do not understand, for the book does not teach me all;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but you know masters well enough about many great things, and about that which is present and wanting.</start_of_turn>
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Find nine works, and a new instrument, for the descending of strange things that arise in this art.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the towels do not grow from limbs or are made of anything other than by means:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Or by land or by water, or from some other place;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	Or by land or by water, or from some other place; and that which leaps forward by itself, that is an arrow transfixed in the flesh, and leaps nevermore.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it until the flesh is rotten, and rejoice at its issue;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it is pierced in the bone, and it cannot be extracted, if you leave it there a few days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And thus it leaps, and if it does not leap, if it has pierced through all that is subtle, as long as the wound has been widened, then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the fragment is caught in the bone of the shoulder, and comes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and leave no other signs that I have said before to the patient: if you do not take it out, but leave it as it is until it is equal again after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the splinter comes up to the marrow, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the splinter is not firmly fixed in the bone only, and does not go beyond the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the splinter is not firmly fixed in the bone only, and does not go beyond the surface, and remains loose in the patient for a long time, without any obvious accident, if the inflammation swells up, it will be troublesome.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is not firmly fixed and cannot be extracted, if it has been embedded too deeply, as I have said; then treat the limb until it is healed
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the splinter is returned to the bone if it cannot be seen, if the wound has healed entirely;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you sense it, if the limb has no visible support;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	if you do not find support by the width of the wound and by the depth of the arrow
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve or blood vessel, if the wound is so great.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there is an ear in the arrow that holds it,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If the bone that is hooked by a joint moves away from the muscle that you pull,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	Then it breaks or tears the cartilage of the bone, as long as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And take great care that you do not break the bone, that you only pull out the cartilage.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not do it once, if the limb remains bent even after you have pulled, then draw it out once more, for extraction is joyful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the discharge of blood opposes you, if you recall what we have said about the treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision of the vein and the vein, and put in place as you will there where the arrow went out with danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or if he is open or closed, firmly or slightly; and put the patient in the position in which he was when the arrow went out of him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because that is the greatest aid that there is, and if you do not know how, look at what they show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The bandage that comes from another place, or it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The swelling therefore increases so much that the nails can no longer bear it, and then it must be removed: if it happens at this moment.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you round your hand around it as much as it enters the bone, and dilate the bone, then extract it.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be extracted, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out.</start_of_turn>
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if the splinter is firmly stuck, it is necessary to grasp it all at once.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if the splinter is firmly stuck, and you see an instrument that can grasp it, grasp it immediately, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the point of the splinter gets caught in the hole of the instrument; and then pull firmly,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the splinter is firmly caught, if the instrument has a pointed end that can enter, to make it easier to extract.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the wound is surrounded, then it is necessary that you grasp all the surrounding flesh or the venom is there, if you know.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound if it is possible.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the wound leaks blood or pus from the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close, and you know it, cover it immediately.</start_of_turn>
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and keep the wound covered and the nerves, and then extract it, and then suture the wound, if necessary.</start_of_turn
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment is until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the nails from which we treat the wounds are similar to the beak of an oyster, and thus is this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are various kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the wound
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the tip is like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For to relieve the tip of the arrow, if it is thus shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	its shape like pliers to grasp and pull out if it is thus shaped.
des voinnes dou cors communes	it is common.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	it has or has not head or root,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	It is known that: the batons following the ears, which are close to the painful parts.
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the veins which are in the temples appear;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins which are in the armpits, which are close to the armpits, are called "aspirations".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the back of the head near the ear;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the armpits which are swollen;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the armpits which are swollen; and the veins which are raised above the mouth, which are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the armpits which are swollen; and the veins which are swollen below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly known are in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic [dislocation], and is on the left side of the costus [breastbone], and they call it the people "chief of the head."
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the other is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and brachial [dislocations].
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it the people "chief of the head"; and the brachial is either on the left or right side of the costus.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the people "chief of the head"; and it is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And that is the one which is always seen, which openly manifests above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saving one is the vein which is between the thumb and the index finger, and if there are two of them;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the limb and where the bone is, there are two veins: one if it is beside the elbow of the left side of the costal cartilage,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one runs at the ankle of the right side of the costal cartilage; and the vein which is called “nesse”, which is at the ankle of the other costal cartilage;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other limb are two veins close to those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to produce old purges and diarrhea.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the blood, as I have told you, is that you restore the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the limb or the veins are rough; then stretch the patient’s neck with a finger,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	As long as the veins open behind the ears toward the head, depending on the chief:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	since their root approaches the head, whenever the pulse is felt at their root, if it signifies a suspicion of an embolism.</start_of_turn>
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and pierce the vein down to the bone, and then keep your hand over the entire upper part of the vein,

Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the two arteries that are in the temples, if it is like an ancient emigration,

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the front vein is just as important as the blood from the cephalic vein, for there are diseases of the face of old age, such as migraine and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as when a vein bursts.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called the "forceps," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or something else, and let blood spurt out as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then deliver to the patient the neck, and bind the vein until it is whole and never more with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Whatever, let the flames be too strong; and the same through, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the veins that are in the armpits if it helps with the eyes, and with the tongue, and with the redness, and with the swelling in the fat, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their blood if it is that the patient pulls his head to the side by twisting any thread, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the same, and let the blood flow freely, a long distance from the flame, because there is no hair.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make a drain of blood, as much as you are able, and then bind it up, and hold it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood of the vein does not matter if it is like water, and in sobriety, and in fevers,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	if it is like emigration and redness that comes to the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and if the patient’s pulse is tight, then strain his neck with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the burning flame slowly long, and hold it against the liver in the space between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open easily, and it will not begin to heal now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	do not go too far in incisions, and do the evacuation of blood according to your need, then bind it up for a night, for it is often restored after treatment;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the armpits helps to stop the swelling of the spleen, to the beginning of mumps, and to the mouth of diseases, and to swelling, and to corrosions, and to herpes, and to tumors.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	When the quality of the blood is that the patient strains his collar alternately from one side to the other, as we have said before.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	or the master is standing over the chief of the patient, and the patient sits on one seat,

que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Then repeat the process on the other side, then loosen the ligament and strain lightly the middle veins,
De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the limbs above helps to cause collection in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and ulcers of the tongue, and pain and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And if the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the palm of the hand up, and look at both veins, one on the right side of the hand and the other on the left
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you will know them by their blackness, and because they have small black veins running through them:

si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If the greatest of the shoulder bones is displaced downwards, and the same happens with three veins which are below and beside, for this is a treacherous method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the blood below the tongue the tongue will hang down.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the blood of the head, and this is at the widening of the throat, and there are diseases of the eye, and there are diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the air is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and he stretches out his tongue, and looks towards the outside of each shoulder, he sees a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Healthy then, both of them, and do not advance too eagerly, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins which we commonly cauterize are usually healthy in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by pricking at their base with a fine lancet, like a twig or olive branch if you cut deeply, and is called “anesil.”
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the fire cautery is known to be mild and wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And must be used to open wide veins filled with great blood that appears, containing great blood and turmoil.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	It is the olive-like flame form:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for safer veins, or where there is clear yellow blood.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, if it helps, has diseases such as nausea of the throat, or cold, or pain, or belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is useful to the patient that he remain calm, and that he abstain from eating from the artery which is nauseous.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	and if he grasps the artery, and blood flows out, if the physician is vigilant, as I have said.</start_of_turn>
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be afraid of the flame, but should seize it as if by an animal.</start_of_turn
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the vein does not open visibly, if you must extract it, and tie off another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you desire no blood to spill, or you leave the vein closed in the arm: it will open visibly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the burn at the flame will vanish, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the limb of the bloodstained, if you must extract the limb, that you touch the limb as long as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the limb endwise, and then bind the arm, and clamp the vein with the flame anew.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware that you do not cut the artery when you see the limb swollen, for that is the artery: close it off immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see blood flowing upwards like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor frothy, consider that there is no artery involved.</start_of_turn>
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry and place your hand along its length, then tighten your hand if it is not bleeding, for this has happened many times before.</start_of_turn
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	The arm is held close to the body, and the hand is left loose, without moving the patient; and if there is fear, do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it is not stained, and it is painful, and the doctor is not present, if the artery bursts, because the head of the bone is pulled back; then hold it still without touching it.</start_of_turn>
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a support of mustard seeds, and make it, and take half of it and put it on well until the other half;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it is not stained, that is good; but if it is, as we have said, powders that stain blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	The wounds do not bleed excessively in many cases, except for the small vessels of the wound and the tension of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood of the vein helps to hold the wound shut so that it heals properly, and from the shoulders to the wrists
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basal and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary that the vein should be wide enough to allow the nerve to pass without being compressed, and if it is too narrow, the nerve will be compressed.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And he swells and his sanity is either seized or gone, and by chance cannot be healed.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some way by its subtlety, it is certain that you must take away its sensation from the instrument; and keep the nerve away from your sight.</start_of_turn>
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it is too long.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it brings blood without pain, and helps the veins.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is recommended to cauterize with olive oil fire or with mirtin fire, for these are the safest of all veins, because they do not contain nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to test the fire first, and do not be discouraged if it does not work the first time, and we repeat it.</start_of_turn>
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, it happens to burn someone’s face the first time, but that does not matter.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thinking.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood is not to be shed except for the preservation of life,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	...and to prevent diseases from arising.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	or in one of the two veins which are or should be: namely, the cephalic, facial, and basilar
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the sign of replenishment appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And if one must renew the first joint or the third, after a quarter or two of an hour.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing which is administered for diseases has no definite measure, but whenever there is a need for joint or nut, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and must not be renewed more than twelve and a half years, and a woman who is pregnant must not be treated for more than four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Must not be treated those who are older than sixty.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	When others see health restored in any way, even if it be by a slight laxation of a hernia,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	...if it has the strength of madness retained, so that the veins do not draw out the intestines with the nourishment that is in the principal parts.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	...neither those which are too lean from meat, neither those which are too dry, neither those which are too fat, nor watery;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	...and if after a violent passion, vomiting, and swelling of the belly, multiplied by an abundance of eating and drinking, and this in the midst of all the virtues, or by some weapon or poison.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtlety the humors, if they are not great, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have any at your disposal.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then give a lukewarm bath, if nothing else hinders you, to subtilize the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and apply a warm compress to the area below the pit of the stomach, as we have mentioned before;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard against this work, pain, luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And so they lie bound and joined, and let the healthy side be above that which is to be sawn off, and wipe with the hands once or twice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then draw out the thread from the middle, for when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot be corrected without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	Then wipe the limb with the hands, until the veins swell, and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the healthy side with a little oil, then put his left hand over that vein below the limb a little or where it seems healthier,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	The wound did not bleed and did not yield to the incision.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like cords in the air, and if they are of such sort as are full of wind,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when one sets the flame to them, when one takes away the flame, they do not open the vein, and thus is this;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the wound is too deep, because of this it is necessary that the physician be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, it is good; if not, if it recurs again, do another scar there or in the neighborhood, if the wound is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	If the wound is inflamed and the patient is groaning, if you leave it for an hour or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	because in this way there will come swelling; do not enter or bathe, then repeat the bleeding if it clots again.

et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And in the work one must be cautious, even when the wound is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the wound inflamed, do not renew the bleeding, and put on a little oil bandage, for it softens the pain of blood, and is mild in this limb the oil that is on it.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and give the oil bandage in such way as to stop the course of the blood.

Many times there is swelling and discharge at the root of the arm: put your hand there, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of your hand, that is an evil sign.

Listen well that you put nothing on it of what we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but it makes it swell dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If it is black without, leave it black as long as it is red; if you see it large, leave it until it is slight; if it is too thick, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it must be done for the blunt and firm, and having the need for bloodletting, we make the wound larger and the flame greater;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the weak one, do the opposite, and keep it healthy somewhat, and do it more gently, not by pricking;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	this method of bleeding saves from the loss of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than blood that lasts a long time does not last long.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for those who have swelling in the groin, it is advised to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is nauseous, take two or three times as much blood.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, give beforehand the sick soft bread soaked in must or honeyed syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant syrup.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he vomits blood after the evacuation of blood, it is advised that he should drink broth of barley and fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the bladder.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he sees his arm swelling up again, and gets better once, if it is swollen by a great amount of blood, he must rise up and rise up immediately, in proportion to the quantity of his continuous virtue.

et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not believe me when you see the limb slip from its place the second time, and the wound is closed, that you must press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the limb widely, for this would be bad;
