et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on it immediately some water, and press lightly.</start_of_turn>
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not bind it tightly, as long as the incision is calm.</start_of_turn>
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to draw out blood the second time, if the same is in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.</start_of_turn
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The arm vein is bloody at the root because it is made up of many small veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the color of the blood is that of warm water, as long as the vessel is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound firmly, so that the vein opens well, and then let it pass through without widening or lengthening;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	or if it cannot be passed through without causing harm, let the hand remain in warm water, and leave the blood to flow until enough has bled;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	If it is thus, if you do not withdraw your hand quickly from the hot water, for there is more in the laver than in the heat.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	If so, the blood of this vein is more precious than all the arteries and nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The saliva of the right hand is worth against all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is visible.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the limb hangs by the skin, and if you support it with all your might, if nothing is broken;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	it will not cause you much harm, for the nerves are already detached from flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then put the limb into warm water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if you put oil and lint on the wound to stop bleeding, and then make a dressing.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have said concerning the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the armpit is worth for all the diseases which are in the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	if like the disease of the mouse, retention of flowers, disease of the veins, and of old wounds and limbs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this blood is that if the patient is in great pain, and wipes over the wound until it is dry,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And he must hold the thumb under the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and from under the foot go out drops of rain.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	The limb is pale or has large drops of rain, or at the ankle, that the pulse is weak.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you see the limb pale under the foot, if you are aware of nerves that are swollen, and the limb travels as if grasping; and let the flame be extinguished.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be cured, if you reset the limb in water, and let the vein discharge well.</start_of_turn
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the limb must be reset for the first time, if it is repeated a second time shortly afterwards, because the limb is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt, as we have said, and take the other limb equally alongside.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth as much as the pain of the hip, when it is for blood that is clotted.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its blood is if the patient is between or in water, and it strains from under the ankle to the knee.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it does open, whatever way you may try, and even through and through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is better to leave it closed, for its blood is thick, and it is more easily closed by the hands of a layman.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it [the vein], if some rain of blood opens or comes out, and towards the little toe, and guard against the nerves.</start_of_turn
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do as much pressure with blood as you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind; it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
Des sainies de ventouse	Des sainies de ventouse.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made from horns, or hair, or leather; and the application of the ventouse should be done in the following manner: either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting alone.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this application of the ventouse which is cutting alone should be done in the following manner: either it is with great heat, or with a little heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the exhalation which is made by cutting and extracting blood if it is done in twelve and a third hours of pain.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	And the one is all over the head; and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and there are three others in the ribs of the neck; and the vein of the tongue is exhaled through the mouth
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the exhalation of the spleen; and the exhalation above the kidneys;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the windsucks swell the armpits; and the windsucks of the thighs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the windsucks of the calves; and the swelling does not concern blood, for there are many veins scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	Therefore it does not matter if one makes a bleed of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	It is not necessary to bleed for any ailment that comes from an excess of blood; for as long as the patient's body is void of any swelling, it is not necessary.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity demands it for illnesses, or by custom, if the attendants are seized with a sudden spasm in the beginning or at the end, and in every tension;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they must vomit, have a heavy head.</start_of_turn>
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who have swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the collar, and dark circles under their eyes.</start_of_turn>
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a spit of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and vomit blood.</start_of_turn
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if I have such ones who think, and see by nut blood and sweat and moisture and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is covered in moisture like blood and sweat, we command them to be exposed for two hours after sunrise.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The patient’s blood is of great help in the treatment of the chief … which comes with these blisters; and we command that it be evacuated only after the removal of all the flesh;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	provided that the bloodletting of the cephalic vein has been performed.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not permissible for me to advise anything except for one who has a cold complexion in use, or who has a rash, because this brings great discomfort to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason I advise only those who are in good health, who do not have or have recently had any serious illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if anyone suspects that they are becoming unwell, it is better to put on the suction cup a little lower down due to the risk of complications.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suction cup is better at the edge of the wound than at the center, because it avoids both the chief blood vessels and the nerves, and for this reason it is more effective for wide wounds.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And at a fracture of the windpipe by the tonsils, and at vomiting, and at repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it must be known that if it [the windpipe] is held too tightly, it will cause obstruction of the belly or the stomach or the chest
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The winds blow cold as cold as the collar of a coat when it is cold, and causes pain in the head, and swelling and pain in the root of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And sometimes the mouth opens by itself, and the blood does not stop flowing.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow loud in the mouth if it is caused by a disease of the mouth, and by corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the cause of the health of the teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the south blow loud in the mouth if it is caused by heat and swelling
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the south blow loud in the mouth if it is caused by a disease of the mouth, and by corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the cause of the health of the teeth.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The winds of the south blow loud in the mouth if it is caused by a disease of the mouth, and by corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the cause of the health of the teeth.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to fear too much pain, for the flesh is subject to char, and knows bones and nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	If there is a wound on the buttocks, it causes swelling at the root of the bone, and diseases of bones and nerves, and it is necessary that the dressing be large and firm, and that it adhere well; for if it is too loose, it will break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds of the legs swell widely, because they draw blood from all over the body, and cause ancient pains of the rains, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and swell the flowers; and are in place of the two buttocks, and the two ankles, and all of them gradually consume the body after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is as follows: if you apply it at first glance, and with steady pressure, and place it firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see blood tinged with flesh and the redness of blood; then rejoice, and remove the suction cup, and take care of the body, for there are many who have suffered from excessive tension and clear pores: if you only cut once, you will make large wounds and a deep wound; do so gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not large, if you must cut once, do so cautiously at first to dilate the blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is very thick, if you must cut three times; and when our wings draw blood, even a little, if we only cut once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	If our veins burst with blood, if we repeat the process too often; if it is not feared, if the pain intensifies, if the wound is perceived too deeply,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	Then it is proper for one who has thick skin and is tough, and who has numerous pores, that you order the application of warming and dissolving liniment.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If this is the case, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkinseed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in ivy, with rosemary oil, or thyme, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the superfluous moisture is great and cold, take oil of marigold, or balsam, or oil of ivy, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	If the skin is tight and has large pores, do not apply oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is permissible to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or elderberry water, or cucumber water, or pearl water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it easily rises, or of elderberry and sumac, and the like.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excess of phlegm rise from wine strong, or from salt water, or from decoction of fennel or chamomile, or from other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and do not remember to be healthy after the bath before and after the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after the bath.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and must know when to bathe and when it is necessary to bathe.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware those who are sickly are cold and if they are too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If he grasps cold things, such as pomegranates, radishes, lettuce and milkweed, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eats barley bread, fat meats, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	and he who has a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and scented wine which is between autumn and spring, and eat little, and drink wine and eat fats and herbs and spices.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he feels a draft, he should drink more than he eats.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is fitting to give some comfort to the patient at all times, neither before nor after the incision, in order to soothe the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Or do it cautiously without fail, but do not let anyone who is unskilled handle it.</start_of_turn>
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The incisions which are to be made are those which are made upon the liver, and the spleen, and the foot, and upon the belly and the belly-button and the armpits and the groin, for these limbs do not suffer from incision on the outside.</start_of_turn
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and only when it is necessary to draw blood from limb to limb.</start_of_turn
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	If as we place on the limbs what is needed to drain the swelling which is in the limb; for to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, if as we place compresses on the belly and on the buttock to diminish the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, if by its virtue it attracts the swelling, or dislodges the stone from its place
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and make it swell up when it is placed on the liver and the heel when there is retained moisture,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these compresses are administered empty so as to soak up as much as possible; and never are they administered together with fire, and never are they applied with pure water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	If there is pain in diseases of the chest, and in such a manner that the patient has a fever and vomiting, or has taken herbs that are codependent on this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the applied ventouse is like this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And has two large handles and a half palm of thickness, and has or costs at the center a small hole, as to push out an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be of leather, so that it does not burn the patient when put on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there is in the middle a twig of willow or iron, to hold the poultice firmly in place.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there are great and small ones according to the illness and the nature of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the swellings of the limbs are different from those of the organs, and the lean from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one put this poultice upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take hold of the loop of thread or line, and put it into the ventouse through the hole that is in the ventouse.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If it is grasped at the bottom of the ventouse so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then put it on the limb, and hold it either on the hole that we mentioned earlier, or on the opening that we have seen; and if when we look, if there is vapor, we remove the ventouse.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And grasp the thread firmly as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction which is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all its sharpness, there is no bulge or perforation, and is administered only when it is clear of sharpness; and is placed upon the limb only as little as possible.
et c’est li forme:	and thus is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suctions are administered only in limbs where we cannot place a ventouse because of their small size, such as the ears and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the nakedness of hair, if for example nails or teeth, and other things of that kind;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And if you find nails that are soft and smooth, without any trace of nails, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them in water that is lukewarm, until they are limp, and do not have anything in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then either wash with vinegar and sponge, then scrub the limb until it is red, and put on the nails.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are flat, and hurt, if it is possible to put on a sponge or a suction cup, do so, for it is worth doing afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb easily, then with some force, move it well, and then release it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb remains too long after the swelling has subsided, if moist, let a cold drape of linen rest upon it until the swelling has gone down.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swelling persists, apply a broken glass or bandage, and similar things, until the swelling has gone down
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you remove half of the barley grains and leave them on the limb until they are burnt out, which will stop the bleeding now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you are in greater need, take other precautions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if these precautions are not sufficient, if you can, rub the limb with fresh blood, or insert a needle into it until the hair is gone.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then put them on, and as soon as they feel blood, if they bleed;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they bleed, if you can, sprinkle over a little alum and some lint, or charcoal, if you wish.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Ci comence li livre des brisures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen well, dear son, for this chapter teaches you things that no former book or letter has ever recorded;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason is it strange in our land, for I have never found such a thing before;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except by the wisdom of the ancient books, or because I have studied so much that I have learned the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	I have described it in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are brought into play, as I have done in the preceding chapters.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book are the sum of words and the chapters or the learned man puts his understanding into them, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proved learn and learn this noble art, and learn from others.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion or swelling comes to none of these, if you command that the patient hasten the healing of the ailment from one side and from the other, nothing must hinder him, if it be from weakness of the body, or childhood, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if he is not very strong, or too cold; and eat cold dishes, that is to say cold soups, broth of oil and garlic, and drink no wine, eat no greasy foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins with blood, until you are sure that the after-effect of the cautery is not too great, nor swelling of the limb; if the patient recovers before the first day, return to the former treatment which he used.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you command that the patient be given no meat which makes great swelling, or which has viscosity, if it be like wheat flour in water, and rye, and testicles, and meat, and fat, and fish, and strong wine, and similar things.</start_of_turn
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part of its nourishment, it returns muscle and more quickly breaks the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones that break from marrow and cracks do not mend well together according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, just as if they were too tender, like bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no remedy, hold over the fractured bone, that is, strong tensions that are bound and unite the limb together, as much as it is firm as before; and do not move from its place, and for this reason it is recommended to nourish with great meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at the shoulder there is its engine, and its proper instrument in restoring it, according to what it remembers from its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known by the breaking of the bone by that which it is twisted, and opens well by pulling, and by pressing of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no dislocation, and no great pain, if there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have dislocation, or fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not possible to move the limb only by hand, but medicine is added afterward, then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	If the fracture is split through the root, and if these are the two parts of the joint, it is necessary to hold them firmly in place now, as well as the incisions that are to follow;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	if there are abscesses around it, if they are left untouched, as long as the abscesses are not calmed down;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it firmly and gently, and take care that it is not heavier to restore it than before, or that there are pieces left; and then hold it firmly once again afterward.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones, if they extend from a third to a half of the limb, if it is the hand or foot, or at the wrist if it is a small limb, or at the elbow if it is two strings, or at the hand and foot;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are freed, if you leave by all means the additional swelling in their place, and keep that in your work there comes no further damage or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and carefully support the joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if he seems that it is not well: if the wound closes well, and does not tighten too much, do not press as do some who make it come about by their work at the incision and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is stiff, if he stays well with the patient, that he does not move, neither watch nor sleep, neither turn, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	take great care that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you can make him put it into partial use when he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it properly aligned, so that torment does not arise when you restore it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and as to the limb which is broken, it is like that which I have told you.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The breaks of the limb are various in small and great size and shape.</start_of_turn
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and the like: if you cover them with linen cloth which is soft and flexible.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for those which are large, such as buttocks and thighs: if you cover them with a wide and hard cloth, because the large cloths embrace the whole great limb and constrain it equally, so that there is no slackness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then put on tight stockings, that is two or three according to the size of the limb, and constrain your hand one palm to the whole limb, and go up to the break and constrain less, that the break then lets go a palm of the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb somewhat, so that you take a great part of the limb, then take another limb, and turn the tight bandage over the limb break;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then draw towards the lower part of the break, and strain moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we said earlier.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the layers of skin some strips of linen or cloth, until they are all even, and then bind everything up above. That is, bandage, and then put your thumbs well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, if put on above something soothing the abscess, which hardens the swelling, and leaves it alone for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain on your thumbs, and let them be half as wide as a broad thumb nail, or of a fist from which you make nails, or of barley straws, and let them be as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the one who puts on the bandage should make it larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as is appropriate for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then is strained on the edges as you did at the first hour, and then bind under a thread subsequently, as was done at the first hour on the bandage;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is tight underneath, that is less; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen wool.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make them bind linen thread too tightly, this is a great mistake, for the thread will not be even if it is too subtle, and I advise that there be at least a finger's breadth of space between the knots.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is nauseated by the blows of the stones after the stretching of the limbs, put some sponges of linen or coarse cloth on them so that they do not bruise.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When there is a wound with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will speak of the treatment of that later.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	The wounds that he cannot bear to endure from these stars shall break all the limbs at the first moment.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	When the limb is large, he cannot bear to put these stars there except after five or seven days, or more, according to the severity of the wound that comes out;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and when the old wounds remain to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour that adheres to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and put this confection, not too thick not too thin, and use it. This is the common method of dressing that restores the fracture in various positions, and is suitable for both women and young children, because it is neither too tight nor too loose.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley and linseed and ivy and asafoetida and gum arabic and mugwort, in the amount of X; myrrh and aloes, in the amount of V; chamomile, in the amount of VII; and mix them together. If the patient’s complexion is hot, use this dressing, because it is of good composition and restores the fractured bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other method of reduction worth torsion: take mugwort and vismut, 10; rue, mirre and aloes, 78; acacia, 5; arnica, 10, and grind well, and confit with water or plenty of eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Other method of reduction worth torsion: take mugwort and vismut, 10; rue, mirre and aloes, 78; acacia, 5; arnica, 10, and grind well, and confit with water or plenty of eggs, and administer. Take new linen, moisten with oil and boil, and apply to the sore. These plasters do not restore immediately, but are good for soothing post-burn pain, and properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other method of reduction that restores fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial pell leaves, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Other means of restoring the fracture of the bone and removing the remaining abscess. Take root of vismalve, chamomile, violets flowers, wheat flour, and from chescune one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with moist coriander water, or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Other means of support more forceful than the first, when a hard abscess comes with the restoration of the limb. Take root of vismalve, flaxseed, barley, melilot, violets and chamomile flowers, all of one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that he puts nothing on the broken limb except a little wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between two things neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen commands that we put something dry on the broken limb to restore it, such as mirre and aloes and incense and the like.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is good for wound and pain: take mugwort and chopped onions, or willow buds, and mustard, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bones of his limb have not moved; if you do not loosen it by hand for a while.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling or itching, if you are hasty, loosen the dressing and place the limb in water; take a light bandage and a wet sponge, and immerse in water, until the itching ceases and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind up with a nut, until you are certain of the wound has healed.</start_of_turn>
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And rest the inflamed limb, and relieve the pain, then reapply the bandage and a little dressing, and do not bind too tightly; and be gentle until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around a bone, and if the limb returns to its original position as before, you must immediately immobilize and support it, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If it does not recover the limb in the way we have mentioned, do not remove it for two or three days, or five or seven; and in no case leave it for twenty days, as we have seen, until the swelling has subsided and the limb has returned to its natural position.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore, you must restrain it more strictly than before, and nourish the limb; as I said before. And if you see that the limb dries out more than usual, do not give it any nourishment;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	The waters of hot spring rise, whenever you loosen them, every time a third time or more, they split a limb like a thread.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, indeed, it loosens the bones of the limb, and it makes them limp thus that the limb returns twisted: that is bad, and if the work is feeble, and I see nothing but to leave it and treat it violently.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaks.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking, and various figures, and the causes are diverse;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone is broken throughout to the syfac which is the marrow of the bone, as if made by a saw or a fist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a fracture of the haft.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For when the spear pierces the bone from below in a piercing fashion, and is called this kind of fracture an "absolute fracture"; and is the wound of these major or minor fractures.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fracture or break of bone, or fracture of bone on bone, or swelling on bone, or other similar things.</start_of_turn
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the joint which is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is close to the bone as much as a hair, and the fracture is small, it is called a "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made or caused by a stone, or by a thorn, or by anything similar, and it brings the piece of bone forward, as when coals are placed on the embers; if the bone is split in two.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this is more common among those who have or have had moist bones, like children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are numerous ways in which these breaks happen, when small pieces are loosened from them like these; and I will speak of them in detail.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all these breaks due to the detachment above them, and the inquiry of wounds, and the corrupt flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The blood vessel is known by this, that when one has discovered the bone, and has wiped around it, if the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient's well-being, and if you see no other mishap, such as vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes becoming yellow and flushed, and other similar things, if it does not recover without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an impending accident, and you hope for health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when it comes to the swelling which appears first, and which is in the armpit, if you can remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the muscle which you must remove
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day from the bone which must be removed, then the tissue of the bone will be corrupted, and there will come the accident which we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the breaking of the bone comes up to the tissue which covers the brain, if you can make the fractured part flexible: and it is that you take hold of the head of the patient who is groaning, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more severe than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the blood drains from a vein, or an abscess bursts, he should use what he can to hold it in place; and fill the wound with soft cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And keep the wound closed until the swelling has subsided; and be sure that there is no further bleeding. Then, once the swelling has gone down, turn the bone to its natural position; this is done in two ways: one way is if you grasp the nail of the wound firmly at the front, and the other is like this:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another incision more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have a variety of different sized wounds, some wide and some narrow, and some pointed and some blunt, and on a lighter wound, do not cauterize the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through, do not make the wound deeper than necessary; and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass through the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if there is bone left in the wound of the thickness of the bone, if you have several punctures you will remove all of the bone.  This is the form of two of these punctures:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through bone is that you put on one tarer over the bone, and turn your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then you remove the tarer from another place a little later, and do the same thing all around, and cut out the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do it more skillfully than you could, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought out the bone from your hand, or from any instrument which you have like nails, pincers; and keep your fingers away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have grasped the bone firmly, and treated it, if it is possible, reset the abutment that has come loose from the bone with any other instrument resembling an incisor, but it must be more tense and subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it does not come loose any of the small bones, no nails, if the bones are slightly fractured; then cure the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more useful; and the load is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either that which is fractured or broken open, so that when you have uncovered that part, put back the tip of this lenticular incisor, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut too deep, for the part which is hollow in these costs lies close to the bone; then hold with a little mallet above, so that you may compress the bone gently, and take care of the cloth which is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is open to the bone, if the bone is slightly fractured, for we must move the bone gently, without fear or pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if a bone breaks through the skin does not pierce completely, and is only slightly fractured by its underside, there are small pieces; if you can rejoin the fracture, and remove the splinters with a blunt scraper, which you must have in various quantities, to mend each limb as well as possible, according to the work and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is before great pain, and afterwards more subtle, and does not cease to do this until it is well.</start_of_turn>

In some other size of capillary and fracture, it is necessary to provide the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not properly learned by anyone who has put his study into this art.</start_of_turn>

puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another bandage doubled in i. or ii., and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first bandage; and do this more gently than you wish, that you do not damage the burn, then administer further i. linen, and do not restrain it more than necessary except as much as the wound allows.</start_of_turn>

et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus. de la routure de la mandibule	De la routure de la mandibule.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement. Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced, that is to say, if it is shifted, if you must administer an extension of the thumb by parts, as much as it is even.

de la forcele	forcefully.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie. de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than any man.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than any man.

de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of bone sticks forward, and does not yield like before, if it persists, hold the bone firm and make what we have said in the loosening of the forceps to soothe the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And never is the limb broken in the middle, but this happens often; but it often breaks from excessive force. And when it is broken in two, if it declines downwards, and causes the patient great pain, and weakness, and vomiting, and by chance blood, and opens the wound in the broken bone, and all that is well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient lies prone upon his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades together, and reassemble the joints of the two ribs in your hands, and subtly force them even in all positions that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should; then place on dressings and stamp upon the external heel of the bandage with fine salt, or some softer substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind firmly over the fracture, if it does not move; and turn the limb slowly backward, and strain gently, and reward after an hour the limb, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you fear that it will slip, due to corrosion or inflammation that comes from within, or pain or swelling, if you hurry, and it slips, remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies prone upon his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades together, and reassemble the joints of the two ribs in your hands, and subtly force them even in all positions that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should; then place on dressings and stamp upon the external heel of the bandage with fine salt, or some softer substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind firmly over the fracture, if it does not move; and turn the limb slowly backward, and strain gently, and reward after an hour the limb, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you fear that it will slip, due to corrosion or inflammation that comes from within, or pain or swelling, if you hurry, and it slips, remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed. And in the case of a broken rib.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Its fractures of the ribs only happen at the large angles behind the back and at the head downwards; and they do not happen for anything else except that they are glassy. And one knows well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And if it is restored, set the fracture equally as before. Then place the bandage and bind it with a pin, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the fracture of the ribs has descended inwards, if the patient experiences great pain, pointing, as if of pleura, for the bone is pressing on the gut; there is vomiting and evacuation of large amounts of blood, which is a serious illness, and the former has put on great effort.</start_of_turn>
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	If any of those things mentioned above are done, it is necessary to administer food that causes the belly to swell, in order to push out the fracture.</start_of_turn>
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for the wounds that remain closed do not heal if they are not opened.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they are opened, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one puts sponges on the limb to soak up the pus, because this is almost a reason; however, there is doubt that the sponge will not pull out the pus from the limb because of the weakness of the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, and put on sponges between the ribs to make the yolk equal all around; then either cure with pleurisin dressing, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the heel, and there is doubt to the patient, if it is necessary to cut above the broken bone, and to put in a dressing; then one must pierce the bone lightly, and draw out the marrow gently, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges. And if an abscess comes up, if put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil on the wound and leave it on; and cure while the bone is being healed, as long as it is necessary.
de la brisure dou col	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the heel, and there is doubt to the patient, if it is necessary to cut above the broken bone, and to put in a dressing; then one must pierce the bone lightly, and draw out the marrow gently, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges. And if an abscess comes up, if put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil on the wound and leave it on; and cure while the bone is being healed, as long as it is necessary. For in the bursting of the heel bone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a bursting of the bone of the heel, and often there is pain; and the same with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to no avail, and you know whether it will be cured or not, if you take warning when you see their hands limp, fleeing and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel pain. Such is death in numerous conditions, and if you move them and feel well when you strain and point, the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured, if we put in cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when something similar happens at the spine, and you know whether it will be cured or not, if you take warning when you see the pieces are softened, and if the accident is what is in the hands or on the back, and there is a violent vomiting and evacuation of matter; and when we have bound it on the belly, if there is still a violent vomiting. Such is death: if we do not work diligently in the cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, if the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that if there is an abscess above, put upon the spine oil of roses or oil of nutmeg of an egg, until it is calmed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.
