And if a bone is fractured, if you must cover over the wound; and fix the bone, then join together the two parts of the wound, if it is large, with a splint, and bandage it, then cure it with ointment until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "break of the jaw", if you have your left thumb in your pouch, and put it equal to the other hand in front, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you need them; then strain it, and if there are fractured bones, if you leave it on, and fix them, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the thigh bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the bone of the thigh is fractured, and if there is no immediate sign of concern at the head [of the bone]; and if it lasts long, and worsens at the root, and brings pain to the patient, swelling and breaking that which is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you place your hand on the [fractured] bone, as long as you are over the fracture; and stretch out what is fractured and the shape of the limb; and if the fracture is only at the head, put it in its natural position, until it is back to its normal shape.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it declines at the root, make the patient rest on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have set the hair even, if you place it on the shoulder joint, then place on a bolster of staff or crook, and hold the limb steady, so that it does not move; and keep the limb still until the hair has grown even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swelling comes, do not touch it, until the swelling has subsided; and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and strain it as it should be strained, if there is no other mishap; and that is the way to do it
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the shoulder blade and the head of the humerus. If it is dislocated, it must be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a fistful of moist earth and restore it in this fashion:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And so take two fingers and bind them together, and lift the patient up on his seat; then place the arm broken over the fist, as far as the elbow, and have the fist bent with a curve, then place something heavy on it or the attendant will extend it forward; then put the hand in its place as it was before, until the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you support the patient on his hip, and bind the arm to his collar, and command the attendants to hold what is on the dislocation at his hands, and the others to hold below all the bones, and extend the shoulders outwards.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the extraction is too strong, if it strains, that is to say, if it pulls out the bristle, on the bristle, and extends one's thumbs to their side. And if the bristle is close to the shoulder, one must know that one must place one's middle finger below the armpit, and the other towards the elbow, below the bristle; and in like manner if the bristle is towards the elbow, one must know that one must place one's thumb lightly, with effort, as long as the bristle is even on both sides. Then one must place the bristle even, if it is possible, and strain, for if the afterbirth does not come away.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If the afterbirth comes, if it does not strain immediately, place upon it a thick cloth soaked in oil of roses until the afterbirth is calmed; then strain, and keep the method of straining as if you placed the bandage over the bristle. Then assemble the limb on the shoulder and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; put on the drape and strain on the shoulder and the limb, so that the limb is steady, without anything hindering it, or without displacing the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, if you use splints, and place on the bristle a splint wider and stronger than the others, and put between the thumbs two spaces as wide as the bristle; then strain on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, stronger and less likely to damage.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the elevation of the shoulder blade and the stretching, as we have said, when you restore the limb promptly and doubt the incision, if you leave it connected until the seventh day, as we have said; then look carefully for two days. If swelling does not occur nor does life regress, or the swelling does not reach the limb, the wound has healed. If necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such thing occurs, if more than two days have passed, and the patient lies on his back with his hands on his stomach; and put the limb in a cushion made of equal wool, and look for an hour or two to see if the limb is not moving, or if the ligaments are not softened; if necessary, by the power of medicine, and do to the limb what we have before recommended, in a moderate way; and when it begins to mend, if it is large. It is customary for the assistant and the limb to be retaken in forty days. And then one must loosen and administer warm baths and ointments for the proper healing. And if the dislocation is stiff and full of blood clots, one must wait to loosen for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	... and if the dislocation is stiff and full of blood clots, one must wait to loosen for one or two months.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of twelve bones, which are called the "femora", of which one is small and is like a nail that supports the pouch; and the other is large and is like a socket, over the small bone. By chance, the large bone only breaks sometimes, or the small, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large bone is broken, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they are both broken together. If only the small bone is broken, if you can, extend it slightly, and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, if you must tighten it more; and extend over one cushion, and keep the pouch of the hand higher than the other, and the small one must be lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arms over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher than the patient himself, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the limb from the shoulder to the wrist, or to the elbow, and one assistant at the other side. And then put it back in its normal position, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, if you put some of them back into their place, and if there is none left to grasp or touch, and you are unable to restore it to its place, if you leave it as it is and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it breaks into pieces, as I have mentioned in the previous chapter; take hold of the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of restoring comes out abscesses, put glue, namely a drape made of rose oil and white wax, that it is neither too thick nor too soft; and bind it loosely, so that the abscesses are appeased. And then bone the wax, and put in the splint of powder of meal with abundance of eggshell, because put the stars, and make the star of the fracture stronger, and one wider than the others; and be careful that it has as many stars as there are joints or limbs in various positions: either that the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and is more strained on the fracture than elsewhere, and all the days less by supporting, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bands be soft and moist on the fracture, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread that is strained be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If other misfortunes arise with the limb, as with itching that arises with the limb, then you must elevate the limb with hot water until the itching subsides; and leave the limb still. Then resume the treatment, and if the tendon is softened and the bone is loosened, and similar things, if necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If it is observed that the swelling will not subside from the limb, because it is too severe, then you must soften it indeed; and leave it alone for some days, until the swelling subsides, and then stretch it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if neither of these things that we have said will help the patient, if not until after twenty days or more, then you must hold his hands to his chest, and keep his neck even, and prevent him from moving and from eating, and let him sleep on his back; and give him food only when the swelling has subsided in thirty days or so, or in twenty days, according to the composition and temperament of the patient.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The bones at the back of the hand, and there are two of them, often break; and it does not come out but pours blood many times.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the hand is fractured or bleeding, if it is suspected that the bones have shifted, and if the patient is sitting crookedly in front of him, then put his hand on the extended cloth and extend the physician’s fingers. Break the fractured bones, and put them in their place; and put on the dressing and the bandage, if there is no further bleeding. Then put on a splint as appropriate; and if necessary cover it with a bandage.</start_of_turn
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the elbow joint towards the belly of the limb, then make a tourniquet of cloth, and command the patient to tighten it at his fractured limb; and then strain from a long bandage, and the splint should be as wide as the limb, and tighten, as it should.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the shoulder, if you command that you place a splint on, and another below in the root, so that the hand is overspread and straight, then you must bind it tightly around the hand, and keep it bound between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break does not come from either side, if it is at the pouch, if you put it even, as it should be; and strain it with the root, and if you see that it does not move when you put on a right-angle splint, and it remains still; and if the break is elsewhere, as in the index or any other, if you put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding the wrist, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the burn, and heal that which comes.
de la cuixe brisie	and if the break does not come from either side, if it is at the pouch, if you put it even, as it should be; and strain it with the root, and if you see that it does not move when you put on a right-angle splint, and it remains still; and if the break is elsewhere, as in the index or any other, if you put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding the wrist, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the burn, and heal that which comes of the bruise.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see it when it bends forward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound with a loop above the fracture and another below.</p>
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs symmetrically; and it is when the fracture is fixed in the bone.</p
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the thigh bone, if either of the limbs above the ankle joint or the other below the fracture. And just as if it were close to the knee, and in general, if either the lower limb or the thigh is flexed; then put the thumbs of both hands under the bone, as much as it is possible to do so according to its natural position, and then put on the dressing and bind, if necessary.</p
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If there is an abscess above, if you leave it calm and then return to your work and your treatment, the binding is done in haste.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	If there is an abscess above, if you leave it calm and then return to your work and your treatment, the binding is done in haste. It is necessary to wrap around the limb with a strong bandage, doubled in two or three places, and to hold the excess taut, then to stretch the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail; and to pass a thread along between the hip and the limb, below the groin, and to bring the thread up at the top; then to stretch the limb and the hip together with the bandage, and to place stars on the abscess, and to place a star on the bone of the limb; then to use eight or nine threads between the limb and the hip of coarse cloth to make the binding even, and to begin to bind making two or three knots on the abscess; and the more you go up the abscess, and the less the strain; and when you have put in eight or nine threads between the limb and the hip, and have tied two stars that are below, then to renew the thread at the top until you see from the nail; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then you must leave it alone, and it will not cause any abscess or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is an abscess above, if it comes loose, and if you address what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them; and if that is not possible, it is necessary to cut the limb open, and drain; and to treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case when one puts in stars, as in the arm and the shoulder; nevertheless, in the restoration that is made, it does not please me the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And the stitches that the bone is restored in, in a day or less or more, according to the diversity of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the rue de Genouil</start_of_turn>
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	The stitches in Rue Genouil break often, but they bleed many times. And if they break, it is not but a tear, or a hole, and there is pain all around, and pain in general, and this is well known.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus, if it is necessary to put things right, equal what is round with its mate, so that they are joined together firmly; then place the bandage, and place a round cushion if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained, then reward all the arrangements that we have said before, as for example incisions and other similar things; and put in every mishap that it may concern him, so that he may be well.
de la brisure de la jambe	And thus, if it is necessary to put things right, equal what is round with its mate, so that they are joined together firmly; then place the bandage, and place a round cushion if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained, then reward all the arrangements that we have said before, as for example incisions and other similar things; and put in every mishap that it may concern him, so that he may be well.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And thus, if it is necessary to put things right, equal what is round with its mate, so that they are joined together firmly; then place the bandage, and place a round cushion if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained, then reward all the arrangements that we have said before, as for example incisions and other similar things; and put in every mishap that it may concern him, so that he may be well. Saiches that there are in the limb have two bones, of which one is called by right "muscle" and the other is called "foscile"; and there is often a fracture as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all done in one.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are fractured together, the limb is twisted throughout.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a marrow bone is fractured, the limb is twisted forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if a large bone is fractured, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it is twisted. Then one must bring extension, and make it even, and bind the bones evenly; however, if the fracture is serious, and there are many pieces, even if the extension is smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, if you take three strips of coarse cloth which wrap around the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the groin to the heel; then encircle with three pieces of linen, which are strong and soft, and bind them together in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not slip downwards or upwards; and this is good; and no one will administer any more medicine which is long on the limb, and if there is swelling, and it is of bone, and puts on the limb; and make the limb still by this binding or any other accident; and move each joint of the limb, to see if there is any other fracture or any other accident; if the cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones due to pain.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture; but in the bones of the forearm there is never a fracture and two are enough; and there is no other cause of death.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the forearm, and you see these bones pressing against each other, if you put such great pain on the limb as if it were going to die, and then put your limb back in its place, where the bones were raised up, then press on the limb until they return to their natural position; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put a little bandage under the bone at the level of the fracture, and bind the limb steadily, and when the pain has subsided, wrap up the limb with cloth and other things as you deem necessary.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is not healed, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or not fractured.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if you restore them as we have said, do two of them with your hand; then put at the end of each break a splint according to the length of the break, and make it wider; and put on the thumb that which I have said, and strain immediately; and if there are three or more, break them, and put on each break a splint according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have said about other breaks, as we have said; and secure each accident as it should be secured.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	... of the break of the thumb bone.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the arm of a woman is broken, if she sits enlarged, then bend her towards the lower back; and hold her there behind; then fill the belly with cotton, and put as much in as a stone; then draw out the woman, and keep her back and front; and then jump the cotton out until it reaches the entrance of the belly, and return the bone with the stone; and when she sees her piss, if the stone is in the cotton, and when she has pissed, she will recover; for she will have made thirty-nine days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see it, take a bladder of Berber, and tie a string around the navel, and pour all the bladder into the belly; then blow through the string until the bladder is expelled: the belly will then return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it as it is for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	When the forearm bone of a man or a woman is broken, or if it is simply fractured, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and these fractures that are not seen often are those which lie in the hands of those who study and use them, and they understand my book. For a fracture means in many cases the right way to restore is through these very methods: so do them.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the limb is broken, take a goose’s neck and put it around the limb; then wrap it with cloth, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be completely healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is fitting for one with a fracture with wound, even if it is great, as with a bone of the thigh or shoulder or the like, that it should be sound now, as the wounds themselves bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, if the rest of the vitriol remains, if you have nothing else, then restore the fracture in this way once more, or that one, for if the pus does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes, if let the restoration be until new morning again, as long as the pus is calmed, and do not touch neither a third nor a quarter, for you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks are open above like a cover discovered, if you must know that you must put your hands lightly on them at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the limb does not extend naturally with your hands, if there is a steel instrument which is about twelve or thirteen inches long, and its width is in proportion to the amount of the wound; for this reason it is necessary at the mire that it should grasp three or four inches, according to what is necessary in the case of a broken bone; and be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not crush the limb during the work.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called "palainche" because it must be placed upon the head of the apparent bone; and once it has gone once, it must be equal so that one meets the other. And if the fracture is slight, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, if you must know that you must hold the head of the bone as long as the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you see the head of a bone displaced by an instrument that can cover it, or by incision or excision, at your peril; then take away what is hindering the bone from snapping and from its rough edges.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is restored, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, the limb is not in its natural position. If you do too much to return it to its place, then moisten it, i.e. cover it with black vinegar, and do so cautiously; and put no cerate or anything else on the wound, for it will cause putrefaction and corruption. Then administer stars when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the dressing thoroughly, according to the quantity of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times this has happened to fools, and it has caused the patient’s death or serious illness many times; or the bruise has been softer and more fluid than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that healing will take place, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to administer stars; but cover the wound thoroughly, with dry cloth, and bind it. And when you see afterwards that the wound is draining blood profusely, if you have put too much on it with vinegar, put on healing salves, such as ointment for wounds and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must keep the limb bound for one hour in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And you must keep the limb bound in part as much as is necessary so that the limb recovers easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the limb persists [dislocated], and it cannot be set right again, with small fragments of bone, because it is necessary that you should attempt to close the wound, and remove all these fragments of bone that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or other kind of corruption, if you must cure it, according to what is said in this chapter above. And when the bone is broken, and is open on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar parts of the great limbs, if you do not treat them, for many times death comes from this; but you must leave them as long as they bleed; by chance it will heal by itself after twenty or thirty days, and then cure the wound if you wish; but if you do not wish, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From the root of the bone that comes out from the swelling.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times we come after the swelling of the bone root, even when it is close to the joint, and it is good to see the shape of the limb; and by chance we cannot make the limb do its natural work.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if it is fresh: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcodea, acacia, and similar others, make sure that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that is astringent or with eggs or with oil; and put them on the wound, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hands for days; and then remove the dislocation, and do it again until the nodulation is bony; or you strain on a well-made piece of flesh; for the property of flesh is that it makes all the swellings under the limb rigid; and if the nodulation has already become hardened as much as stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above is great, and make the apparent surplus; or do not remove it at all, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb is feeble after the dressing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture has been restored, and remains feeble after the limb has been bandaged, if there is any pain: sometimes it is because it was too tightly bound and was not sufficiently loose; or because there are too many bands, and it cannot move smoothly; or because of many wounds; or from too great a movement, not even in its proper place; or because there is blood in the bone, if it is feeble.</start_of_turn>
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient move around and keep the limb firm, until the pain has ceased; and give him baths, and make him comfortable; then put on a poultice over the limb, so that the poultice absorbs the great nourishment, and the wound often suffers from excessive heat, until the nourishment returns to the limb; and bring it back to its natural shape.</start_of_turn>
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after the restoration, and the bone is fractured open, and the limb is deformed, although it does not lose its natural movement: if one does not believe the fools who say it must be fractured anew, and many have done this in our land; this practice is blamed, and it brings great harm, and by chance the patient; although when the swelling and the torture are fresh, if it is considered that they have arisen from hot water, or soft herbs are cooked, as ivy leaves, and roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things; and it makes one.i. emollient plaster, as with good aquaintance, and you take the nourishment of ivy, and confit it with fat of gelatin or olive oil, and make plaster of it; or you take greasy figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that soothe the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And under no circumstances is the bone displaced by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. And provide the limb with rest every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron, if it is covered up to the bone, make an incision slightly deeper; and place padding and a dressing over the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no avail, if it is now to bring back into its place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is late, if by chance it is reset, we shall have pricked the limb at its root; for because of this it must not be moved while it is inflamed: many times this has caused vomiting and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Whenever this happens, if the patient is able to bear the pain, leave the wound alone until the swelling subsides; then raise the limb high and liberally, and move it gently, and cure each limb as it comes back to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint from the root to the wrist.</start_of_turn
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The jawbones.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself in multiple positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entire and accompanied, if you must, immediately restrain it, do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such manner that the minister grasps the head of the patient, and behold the eye that is opposite the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is of a third part; and the other hand must be pushed out, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his mandibles and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And behold the eye that is opposite, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if the two mandibles are together, if they are raised with hot water and oil, so that they remain lightly; do not force to return it, as we have said.</start_of_turn
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth is closed gently, if you put on moist cloths in a circle made of rose oil and beeswax, then bind them lightly with linen threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And the patient lies on his back, with his arms resting between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, neither do they clench, but take hold of the limb gently, until the pain is gone, and keep the jaw closed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then gently move what you see, and do not open the mouth to eat or drink, until the jaw is well closed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jawbones do not wish to return to their place at a single hour, and are not otherwise converted [back to their normal position], if in comes fever and customary sickness, and by chance solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death is the result, in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislodge from the costae without causing damage to the surrounding area, and is always damaged when forced, and one can feel it well.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And if the patient lies prone on his back, extends his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then place the bandage and bind securely, and restrain.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the limb which is towards the knee cannot be loosened; if so, and if it dislocates once, if you leave it in place, as we have said; then place the bandage and bind securely, and restrain, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the meantime, the limb is returned to its place, when it is loosened from its bone.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	The shoulder is dislocated only in two ways: when it slips at the edge of the socket downwards; or when it slips at the edge of the socket upwards; or it slips from the upper part, and this is very dangerous.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	It does not slip behind the shoulder, nor does it slip inwards through the nerves; it slips downwards towards the socket, just as is often the case with those who have a great deal of flesh; or with those who have little flesh, it slips at the point of the shoulder blade, and returns to its place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there are blows or fractures, and the shoulder is dislocated by a thick swelling, and one must take care that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must indeed believe that it is dislocated, as long as you are certain; and then immediately begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when the limb is tilted towards the scapula, and when the bone is twisted, and you will find between their difference the cause of the pain;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a socket, and the scapula pressing on the head of the shoulder, just as if it were a nail; and the patient cannot move their limb in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and thus, if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you will see it immediately when you touch it;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not useless to restore, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the hand of the sufferer be held high, then put the thumbs below the armpit, and hold the joint firmly high up; and the sufferer holds the hand, and stretches it high, since he puts it down; if it comes promptly.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said before, if it is to be known that the patient be bathed in warm water; and he is given soft nourishment and soothing, as decoction of alum and fennel and honey in water, and is given to drink;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then keep the patient reclining on his back, and put under the armpit a cushion of linen equal in size, neither too soft nor too hard, and put the thumb of the hand over the cushion, and keep the shoulder joint firmly in place, and treat the painful hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister holds the head of the patient firmly, if it does not move backwards; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it remains in this manner, follow this method.
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And that you make it present, that is to say, someone who is greater than the patient; and that you place both hands on the sides of the chest, and hold the shoulder below the patient’s shoulder, and stretch the shoulder upwards, so that the patient hangs from the armpit
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister grasps the patient’s hand backwards towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, if you put anything heavy with him, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And thus we must also do in another way: the stone is long like a mustard seed, which must not be too thick or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then put the hand loosely over the patient’s side, but with a soft drape, and let the limb be long enough to reach the fistula; then extend the hand forward and the joint will return to its place steadily.</start_of_turn>
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if all these things do not make it return, if you do this cure: take a fist of three fingers wide and two of thumb, which has the thumb bent to enter into the navel, as in this form:  </start_of_turn>
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay upon the head of the arm a cloth damped with sweat, that it does not bleed the patient; and put the hand of the patient on the seat; extend the arms over the arm of the longth, and support the limb on the arm, and the hand to the wrist, and put the arm over an inch of a span of a finger, and let the hands hang down, or leave the forearm hanging down: the joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way it may be, if you command that you put on the seat a ball of wool equal in size, then put the dressing apart with powdered barley, with incense and alum of egg, upon the whole flank and around, then strain out the moisture from the seat immediately, and draw the limb over the dressing, and embrace the hand to its collar, and let the hands hang down together.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is commanded that he should drink little by little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then drink more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is stiff and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced from its place by moisture, or for another cause, if you must administer cauteries to it twice, immediately and as soon as possible, as it is placed before or alongside the cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it remains loose for thirteen days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot lift the upper arm, then it is likely that the nerves of the shoulder are compressed, stretched or softened; and that the joint will never be stable in its place again.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the dislocation is towards the elbow, and the bones, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the arms, and another support is administered; and it is cured as long as it is done properly.</start_of_turn>
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	If after healing comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later on stiffness, if the patient washes many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later on stiffness, if the patient washes many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If after healing comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later on stiffness, if the patient washes many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	If after healing comes a tingling sensation in the limb, and later on stiffness, if the patient washes many times, until the tingling sensation is gone, and returns to its first state
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And it must be remembered that if it is possible to restore it again after the spasm has passed, grasp the hands with both hands; and extend the arms, and let the hands hang down in accordance with the pain of the joint, front and back, and reassemble the dislocation with its sockets together, or at the root of the bone, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and press from the root of the bone that is loosened.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it by two ministers, if it does not move during extension, then twist the arm from the shoulder downwards; then surround it with a double-folded long and wide cloth.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	When you see that the limb is at its joint, if the limb has been deprived of any oil to lubricate the joint, then stretch the limb until it returns to its place; then keep it stretched until it returns.</start_of_turn>
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	When it is in its place, put on dry patches with egg white, and tighten the limb, and bend the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it thus for some days, then take it off.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if you see that it does not move well, if you rejoin the limb and leave it as it is for some days, until it is firmly set; then you must release it.</p>
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If after the joint has been repositioned, there is pain, and it moves, bathe and massage it well, and press until it is eased; or put on the joint a greasy mutton fat pad, then leave it in place for a day and a night, then take out the bone, and let it enter the bath.</p
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the pad back on, and then enter or bathe; and do this three or four times until it is healed; and if you see that it returns to its place, put on a moist poultice filled with soft wool, and bind it up tightly.</p
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand: the joint of the hand is loosened, and the return is laborious, more so than other joints throughout, so it must be immediately repositioned in its place, while it is loosened, even if the bones are fractured, or if there is contamination of the wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne. Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must watch that it is well positioned; then put the painful hand backwards on a table when extending and returning it.

If it returns now, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of the tendons is appeased by post-traumatic changes, and you leave it in its original position, let it resume its natural course.</start_of_turn>

et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	neither does it harm the patient for as long as the hand is softened, and it cannot strain anything: so that if the nerves are cut, or the veins; if there is no other cause for straining except to cauterize, that is the only thing which is worth doing.</start_of_turn>

des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder do not come loose except for dislocations alone, and it does not come about in any other way; and the joint of the hip is damaged in three parts: front and back, and above and below; the more it is damaged in front, the more it is damaged behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation is such that when one joins the painful limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and opens more the pain of the disease than the normal, and cannot double its knee over the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the cause of this that is taken away by cautery of the abscess, for in this way the head of the scapula comes away from its place.</start_of_turn>
